Capital city of California, United States

**Sacramento**[\[a\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-11) is the [capital city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States "List of capitals in the United States") of the U.S. state of [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California"). The [county seat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County_seat "County seat") of [Sacramento County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_County,_California "Sacramento County, California"), it is located at the confluence of the [Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") and [American Rivers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River "American River") in the [Sacramento Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley"). It is the fourth-most populous city in [Northern California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California"), [sixth-most populous city in the state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population "List of largest California cities by population"), and [35th-most populous city in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population"), with a population of 524,943 at the 2020 census.[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-QuickFacts-7) The [Sacramento metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Sacramento metropolitan area"), with 2.46 million residents, is the [27th-largest metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area "Metropolitan statistical area") in the country.[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-12)

Before the [arrival of the Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas "Spanish colonization of the Americas"), the area was inhabited by the [Nisenan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nisenan "Nisenan"), [Maidu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maidu "Maidu"), and other [indigenous peoples of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California "Indigenous peoples of California"). In 1808, Spanish cavalryman [Gabriel Moraga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Moraga "Gabriel Moraga") surveyed and named the _Río del Santísimo Sacramento_ (Most Holy Sacrament River), after the [Blessed Sacrament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blessed_Sacrament "Blessed Sacrament"). In 1839, [Juan Bautista Alvarado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Alvarado "Juan Bautista Alvarado"), [Mexican governor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_California_before_1850 "List of Governors of California before 1850") of [Alta California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alta_California "Alta California"), granted the responsibility of colonizing the Sacramento Valley to [Swiss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland")-born Mexican citizen [John Augustus Sutter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Sutter "John Sutter"), who subsequently established [Sutter's Fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter%27s_Fort "Sutter's Fort") and the settlement at the _Rancho [Nueva Helvetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Helvetia "New Helvetia")._ Following the American [Conquest of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquest_of_California "Conquest of California") and the 1848 [Treaty of Guadalupe-Hidalgo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe-Hidalgo "Treaty of Guadalupe-Hidalgo"), the waterfront developed by Sutter began to be developed and incorporated in 1850 as the City of Sacramento. In 1852, the city offered its county courthouse to the state of California to house the state legislature, resulting in the city becoming the permanent state capital in 1854 and ushering in the construction of a new state capitol building which was finished in 1874.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-13)

Sacramento is the seat of the [California Legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Legislature "California Legislature") and the [governor of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California"). It is a major center for the California [healthcare industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healthcare_industry "Healthcare industry"), as the seat of [Sutter Health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter_Health "Sutter Health"), [UC Davis Medical Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center"), and the [UC Davis School of Medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Medicine "UC Davis School of Medicine"). In 2013, the Sacramento Convention and Visitors Bureau stated that the city receives 15.3 million visitors per year.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-14) The city is home to [the California Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_California_Museum "The California Museum"), [Crocker Art Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocker_Art_Museum "Crocker Art Museum"), [California State Railroad Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Railroad_Museum "California State Railroad Museum"), [California State Capitol Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol_Museum "California State Capitol Museum"), the [Sacramento Convention Center Complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex"), and [Old Sacramento State Historic Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park").

## History

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: History")\]

Main article: [History of Sacramento, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Sacramento,_California "History of Sacramento, California")

For a chronological guide, see [Timeline of Sacramento, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_Sacramento,_California "Timeline of Sacramento, California").

### Pre-Columbian period

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Pre-Columbian period")\]

[Nisenan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nisenan "Nisenan") (Southern [Maidu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maidu "Maidu")), [Modoc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modoc_people "Modoc people"), and [Plains Miwok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plains_Miwok "Plains Miwok") American Indians have lived in the area for perhaps thousands of years. Until the settlers arrived who would eventually make Sacramento their home, these tribes left little evidence of their existence. Their diet was dominated by [acorns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acorn "Acorn") taken from the plentiful oak trees in the region and by fruits, bulbs, seeds, and roots gathered throughout the year.

### Spanish period

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Spanish period")\]

In 1808, the Spanish explorer [Gabriel Moraga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Moraga "Gabriel Moraga") encountered and named the [Sacramento Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley") and the Sacramento River. A Spanish writer with the Moraga expedition wrote:[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-15)

> Canopies of oaks and cottonwoods, many festooned with grapevines, overhung both sides of the blue current. Birds chattered in the trees and big fish darted through the pellucid depths. The air was like [champagne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champagne "Champagne"), and ( _the Spaniards)_ drank deep of it, drank in the beauty around them. "¡Es como el sagrado sacramento! (It's like the Blessed Sacrament.)"

The valley and the river were then christened after the "Most Holy Sacrament of the Body and Blood of Christ", referring to the Catholic [sacrament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacraments_of_the_Catholic_Church "Sacraments of the Catholic Church") of the [Eucharist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucharist_in_the_Catholic_Church "Eucharist in the Catholic Church").

### Mexican period

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Mexican period")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sutterfort_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sutterfort_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sutterfort_(cropped).jpg) In 1839, [John Augustus Sutter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Augustus_Sutter "John Augustus Sutter") established [Sutter's Fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter%27s_Fort "Sutter's Fort"), which he called [Nueva Helvetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Helvetia "New Helvetia"). In 1841, he was officially granted the land by Governor [Juan Bautista Alvarado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Alvarado "Juan Bautista Alvarado").

[John Sutter Sr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Sutter "John Sutter") first arrived in the area on August 13, 1839, at the confluence of the American and Sacramento Rivers with a Mexican land grant of 50,000 acres (20,000 ha). The next year, he and his party established Sutter's Fort, a massive adobe structure with walls 18 feet (5.5 m) high and three feet (0.91 m) thick.[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-legendsofamerica.com-16)

Representing Mexico, Sutter Sr. called his colony New [Helvetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helvetia "Helvetia"), a Swiss-inspired name, and was the political authority and dispenser of justice in the new settlement. Soon, the colony began to grow as more and more pioneers headed west. Within just a few short years, Sutter Sr. had become a grand success, owning a 10-acre (4.0 ha) orchard and a herd of 13,000 cattle. Fort Sutter became a regular stop for the increasing number of immigrants coming through the valley. In 1847, Sutter Sr. received 2,000 fruit trees, which started the agriculture industry in the Sacramento Valley. Later that year, Sutter Sr. hired James Marshall to build a [sawmill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sawmill "Sawmill") so he could continue to expand his empire,[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-legendsofamerica.com-16) but unbeknownst to many, Sutter Sr.'s "empire" had been built on thin margins of credit.[\[16\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-17)

### American period

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: American period")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sacramento_california_1849.jpg/250px-Sacramento_california_1849.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_california_1849.jpg) Sacramento in 1849, when the city was an economic center of the [California gold rush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush")

In 1848, when [James W. Marshall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_W._Marshall "James W. Marshall") discovered gold at [Sutter's Mill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutters_Mill "Sutters Mill") in [Coloma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coloma,_California "Coloma, California") (some 50 mi or 80.5 km northeast of the fort), numerous gold-seekers came to the area, increasing the population. In August 1848, Sutter Sr.'s son, [John Sutter Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Augustus_Sutter_Jr. "John Augustus Sutter Jr."), arrived to assist his father in reducing his [debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debt "Debt"). The Sutters struggled to contain the effects of thousands of new gold miners and prospectors in the area, many of whom squatted on unwatched portions of the vast Sutter lands or stole various unattended Sutter properties or belongings. For Sutter, his employee's discovery of gold in the area turned out to be a bane.

By December 1848, John Sutter Jr., in association with [Samuel Brannan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Brannan "Samuel Brannan"), began laying out the City of Sacramento, 2 miles (3.2 km) south of his father's settlement of New Helvetia. This venture was undertaken against the wishes of Sutter Sr., but the father, being deeply in debt, was unable to stop it. For commercial reasons, the new city was named "Sacramento City" after the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River"). Sutter Jr. and Brannan had [United States Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army "United States Army") Captain [William H. Warner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_H._Warner "William H. Warner") assigned to draft the official layout of the city, which included 26 lettered and 31 numbered streets (today's grid from C St. to Broadway and from Front St. to Alhambra Blvd.) Relations between Sutter and his son became embittered after Sacramento became an overnight commercial success. (Sutter's Fort, Mill, and the town of [Sutterville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutterville,_California "Sutterville, California"), all founded by John Sutter Sr., eventually failed).

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Sacramento%2C_CA_USA_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento%2C_CA_USA_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento,_CA_USA_-_panoramio_(10).jpg) [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park"), the oldest quarter of the city, grew up along the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") in the mid-1800s.

Residents of Sacramento adopted a [city charter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipal_charter "Municipal charter") in 1849, which was recognized by the state legislature in 1850. Sacramento is the oldest [incorporated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipal_corporation "Municipal corporation") city in California, incorporated on February 27, 1850.[\[17\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-18)

On January 10, 1850, a flood occurred that devastated the city. The rushing waters uprooted homes and drowned livestock. The city was almost destroyed. Due to the efforts of [Hardin Bigelow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardin_Bigelow "Hardin Bigelow"), Sacramento's first elected mayor, the construction of the city's first levee was completed in early 1852 (the city became known as "The Levee City"). However, a month after it was completed, it was breached during the first major storm of the season and the city flooded again. A new levee was built for $50,000, but it also broke, causing more flooding of the city.[\[18\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-19) Between October and December 1850, Sacramento was hit with a cholera epidemic that killed 1,000 residents, including Mayor Bigelow and 17 of the city's 40 physicians. Up to 80 percent of the populace left town.[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-20)[\[20\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-21) On November 2, 1852, a fire known as the Great Conflagration burned more than 80 percent of the structures in the city. It is estimated that the total damage was around six million dollars. Within a month 761 structures were re-built, many of them in brick.[\[21\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-22) In spite of all these hardships the new city's location just downstream from the [Mother Lode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mother_Lode "Mother Lode") in the [Sierra Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.) "Sierra Nevada (U.S.)") proved irresistible, and it grew rapidly during the early 1850s, attracting a population of 10,000. The [Great Flood of 1862](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Flood_of_1862 "Great Flood of 1862") from December 1861 to January 1862 caused the worst flooding in Sacramento's history. In 1861, Governor [Leland Stanford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leland_Stanford "Leland Stanford"), who was inaugurated in early January 1862, traveled to his inauguration in a rowboat.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%27Sacramento_Railroad_Station%27_by_William_Hahn.JPG/250px-%27Sacramento_Railroad_Station%27_by_William_Hahn.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%27Sacramento_Railroad_Station%27_by_William_Hahn.JPG) An 1874 depiction of a Sacramento railway station by painter [William Hahn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Hahn "William Hahn")

The [California State Legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature"), with the support of Governor [John Bigler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Bigler "John Bigler"), moved to Sacramento in 1854. The capital of California under Spanish (and, subsequently, Mexican) rule had been [Monterey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monterey,_California "Monterey, California"), where, in 1849, the first [Constitutional Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(California) "Constitutional Convention (California)") and state elections were held. The convention decided [San Jose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California") would be the new state's capital. From California's statehood beginning September 9, 1850 through 1851, the legislature met in San Jose. It moved to [Vallejo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vallejo,_California "Vallejo, California") in 1852 and [Benicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benicia,_California "Benicia, California") in 1853, before ending up in Sacramento in 1854. During the 1850s the city was [consolidated with](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consolidated_city-county "Consolidated city-county") the County of Sacramento.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-23) In the [Sacramento Constitutional Convention of 1879](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Constitutional_Conventions "California Constitutional Conventions"), Sacramento was named the permanent state capital.

The [Classical Revival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Revival "Classical Revival")-style [California State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol"), similar to the national Capitol, was started in 1860 and completed in 1874. In 1861, the legislative session was moved to the [Merchants Exchange Building in San Francisco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merchants_Exchange_Building_(San_Francisco) "Merchants Exchange Building (San Francisco)") for one session because of the massive flooding in Sacramento. From 1862 to 1868, part of the [Leland Stanford Mansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leland_Stanford_Mansion "Leland Stanford Mansion") was used for the governor's offices during Stanford's tenure as the Governor; and the legislature met in the Sacramento County Courthouse. The legislative chambers were first occupied in 1869, while construction continued around them.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Construction_of_the_California_Capitol_in_1868.jpg/250px-Construction_of_the_California_Capitol_in_1868.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Construction_of_the_California_Capitol_in_1868.jpg) The [California State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol"), built between 1860 and 1874, shown here under construction in 1868

With its new status and strategic location, Sacramento quickly prospered. It was designated as the western terminus of the [Pony Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pony_Express "Pony Express"). Later it became a terminus of the [First transcontinental railroad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_transcontinental_railroad "First transcontinental railroad"), which began construction in Sacramento in 1863 and was financed by " [The Big Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Big_Four_(Central_Pacific_Railroad) "The Big Four (Central Pacific Railroad)")"— [Mark Hopkins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Hopkins_Jr. "Mark Hopkins Jr."), [Charles Crocker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Crocker "Charles Crocker"), [Collis P. Huntington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collis_P._Huntington "Collis P. Huntington"), and [Leland Stanford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leland_Stanford "Leland Stanford"). Both the American and especially Sacramento rivers were key elements in the economic success of the city. Sacramento effectively controlled commerce on these rivers, and public works projects were funded through taxes levied on goods unloaded from boats and loaded onto rail cars in the historic [Sacramento Rail Yards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Railyards "Sacramento Railyards").

From 1862 until the mid-1870s, Sacramento raised the level of its downtown by building reinforced brick walls on its downtown streets and filling the resulting street walls with dirt. The previous first floors of buildings became [basements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basement "Basement"), with open space between the street and the building, previously the [sidewalk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidewalk "Sidewalk"), now at the basement level. Over the years, many of these underground spaces have been filled or destroyed by subsequent development. However, it is still possible to view portions of the " [Sacramento Underground](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park#Old_Sacramento_Underground "Old Sacramento State Historic Park")".

### Modern era

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Modern era")\]

See also: [Urban redevelopment in Sacramento, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_redevelopment_in_Sacramento,_California "Urban redevelopment in Sacramento, California")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Tower_Bridge_Sacramento_edit.jpg/250px-Tower_Bridge_Sacramento_edit.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tower_Bridge_Sacramento_edit.jpg) Built in 1935, [Tower Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_Bridge_(California) "Tower Bridge (California)") connects Sacramento to [West Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento "West Sacramento").

The city's current charter was adopted by voters in 1920.[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-24) As a [charter city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charter_city "Charter city"), Sacramento is exempt from many laws and regulations passed by the [state legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature"). The city has expanded continuously over the years. The 1964 merger of the City of [North Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Sacramento "North Sacramento") with Sacramento substantially increased its population, and large annexations of the [Natomas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natomas,_Sacramento,_California "Natomas, Sacramento, California") area eventually led to significant population growth throughout the 1970s, 1980s, and 1990s.

Sacramento County (along with a portion of adjacent [Placer County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placer_County,_California "Placer County, California")) is served by a customer-owned electric utility, the [Sacramento Municipal Utility District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Municipal_Utility_District "Sacramento Municipal Utility District") (SMUD). Sacramento voters approved the creation of SMUD in 1923.[\[24\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-25) In April 1946, after 12 years of litigation, a judge ordered [Pacific Gas & Electric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Gas_and_Electric_Company "Pacific Gas and Electric Company") to transfer the title of Sacramento's electric distribution system to SMUD. Today SMUD is the sixth-largest public electric utility in the U.S. and is a leader in innovative programs and services, including the development of clean fuel resources, such as [solar power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_energy "Solar energy").[\[25\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-26)

The year following the creation of SMUD, 1924, brought several events in Sacramento: [Standard Oil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_Oil "Standard Oil") executive [Verne McGeorge](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Verne_McGeorge&action=edit&redlink=1 "Verne McGeorge (page does not exist)") established [McGeorge School of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McGeorge_School_of_Law "McGeorge School of Law"), American [department store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_store "Department store") [Weinstock & Lubin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weinstock_%26_Lubin "Weinstock & Lubin") opened a new store at 12th and K street, the US$2 million [Senator Hotel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senator_Hotel "Senator Hotel") was opened, Sacramento's drinking water became filtered and treated drinking water, and Sacramento boxer Georgie Lee fought [Francisco Guilledo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Guilledo "Francisco Guilledo"), a [Filipino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filipino_people "Filipino people") professional [boxer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boxing "Boxing") known as Pancho Villa, at L Street Auditorium on March 21.[\[26\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-Prohibition-27)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sacramento_DSC_0063_%285673641314%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_DSC_0063_%285673641314%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_DSC_0063_(5673641314)_(cropped).jpg) The [Elks Tower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elks_Tower "Elks Tower") was built in 1926 in an [Italianate style](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italianate_architecture "Italianate architecture").

Early in World War II, the Sacramento Assembly Center (also known as the Walerga Assembly Center) was established to house Japanese Americans [forcibly "evacuated" from the West Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") under [Executive Order 9066](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_9066 "Executive Order 9066"). The camp was one of fifteen temporary detention facilities where over 110,000 [Japanese Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_Americans "Japanese Americans"), two-thirds of them U.S. citizens, were held while construction on the more permanent [War Relocation Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_Relocation_Authority "War Relocation Authority") camps was completed. The assembly center was built on the site of a former migrant labor camp, and inmates began arriving from Sacramento and San Joaquin Counties on May 6, 1942. It closed after only 52 days, on June 26, and the population of 4,739 was transferred to the [Tule Lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tule_Lake_Unit,_World_War_II_Valor_in_the_Pacific_National_Monument "Tule Lake Unit, World War II Valor in the Pacific National Monument") concentration camp. The site was then turned over to the Army Signal Corps and dedicated as [Camp Kohler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Kohler "Camp Kohler").

After the war and the end of the incarceration program, returning Japanese Americans were often unable to find housing and so 234 families temporarily lived at the former assembly center. Camp Kohler was destroyed by a fire in December 1947, and the assembly center site is now part of the Foothill Farms-North Highlands subdivision.[\[27\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-28)
The Sacramento-Yolo Port District was created in 1947, and the ground was broken on the Port of Sacramento in 1949.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Ford_rushed_from_Sacramento_assassination_attempt_image_A6320-24A.jpg/250px-Ford_rushed_from_Sacramento_assassination_attempt_image_A6320-24A.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ford_rushed_from_Sacramento_assassination_attempt_image_A6320-24A.jpg) The [1975 assassination attempt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Ford_assassination_attempt_in_Sacramento "Gerald Ford assassination attempt in Sacramento") of President [Gerald Ford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Ford "Gerald Ford") in [Capitol Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitol_Park_(Sacramento,_California) "Capitol Park (Sacramento, California)")

On June 29, 1963, with 5,000 spectators waiting to welcome her, the Motor Vessel _Taipei Victory_ arrived.[\[28\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-29) The [Nationalist Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_Chinese "Nationalist Chinese") flagship docked at the [Port of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Sacramento "Port of Sacramento"), being the first ocean-going vessel in Sacramento since the steamship _Harpoon_ in 1934.

In 1967, [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") became the last [Governor of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California") to live permanently in the city. The 1980s and 1990s saw the closure of several local military bases: [McClellan Air Force Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base "McClellan Air Force Base"), [Mather Air Force Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mather_Air_Force_Base "Mather Air Force Base"), and Sacramento Army Depot. In 1980, there was another flood. Despite military base closures and the decline of agricultural food processing, Sacramento has continued to experience population growth in recent years. Primary sources of population growth are an influx of residents from the nearby [San Francisco Bay Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area"), as well as immigration from Asia and Latin America.

In 1985, Hugh Scrutton, a 38-year-old Sacramento, California, computer store owner, was killed by a nail-and-splinter-loaded bomb placed in the parking lot of his store. In 1996, his death was attributed to the Unabomber, [Theodore Kaczynski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodore_Kaczynski "Theodore Kaczynski").

After acquiring the majority stake in the [Sacramento Kings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings"), the team's new owner, [Vivek Ranadivé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vivek_Ranadiv%C3%A9 "Vivek Ranadivé"), with the help of the city, agreed to build a new arena in the downtown area. With a final estimated cost of $558.2 million, Sacramento's [Golden 1 Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_1_Center "Golden 1 Center") opened on September 30, 2016.

## Geography

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Geography")\]

According to the [United States Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau"), the city covers 100.1 square miles (259 km2). 98.61% of it is land, and 1.39% of it is water.[\[29\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-30)

Depth to groundwater is typically about 30 feet (9 m). Much of the land to the west of the city (in [Yolo County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolo_County,_California "Yolo County, California")) is permanently reserved for a vast flood control basin (the [Yolo Bypass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolo_Bypass "Yolo Bypass")), due to the city's historical vulnerability to floods. As a result, the contiguous urban area sprawls only four miles (6.4 km) west of downtown (as [West Sacramento, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California")) but 30 miles (48 km) northeast and east, into the [Sierra Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.) "Sierra Nevada (U.S.)") foothills, and 10 miles (16 km) to the south into valley farmland.

The city is at the confluence of the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") and the [American River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River "American River") and has a deep-water port connected to the [San Francisco Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay") by a channel through the [Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento%E2%80%93San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta"). It is the shipping and rail center for the [Sacramento Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley").[\[30\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-31)

### Trees

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Trees")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Sacramento_International_Airport_5.jpg/250px-Sacramento_International_Airport_5.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_International_Airport_5.jpg) Aerial view of Central Sacramento and the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River")

Sacramento has long been known as the "City of Trees" owing to its abundant [urban forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_forest "Urban forest"). The city has more trees per capita than any other city in the world.[\[31\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-NPR-32) The first recorded use of the term was in 1855, and it was popular by the early 20th century. It was not always so: it was at first called the "City of Plains" because of the lack of trees, but soon afterward there were [cottonwood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populus "Populus") trees planted, and [eucalyptus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucalyptus "Eucalyptus") varieties were imported to dry out [swampland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swamp "Swamp"). Later, [locust trees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Locust_tree "Locust tree"), and [willows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willow "Willow") were planted along streets, then [elms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elm "Elm"), then [palm trees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palm_tree "Palm tree"), then [fruit trees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fruit_tree "Fruit tree") in the late 1910s.[\[32\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-trees2018-33) It was the first US city to be designated a City of Trees by the [Arbor Day Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arbor_Day_Foundation "Arbor Day Foundation") in 1978.[\[33\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-bee2017-34)

In the early 21st century, the tree cover is well above that of the average tree cover of other major cities in the United States and the rest of the world, with the main species being the [London plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_plane "London plane"). Other species are being introduced to increase diversity and to help cope with the effects of [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") on vegetation in the future.[\[32\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-trees2018-33) [Treepedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treepedia "Treepedia"), a project run by [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT "MIT") using [Google Maps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Maps "Google Maps")' street-view data to calculate tree coverage in cities, ranked Sacramento the greenest city of 15 studied in the US, and third globally, after [Vancouver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vancouver "Vancouver") and [Singapore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singapore "Singapore").[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-35)

A prominent [water tower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_tower "Water tower") bore the slogan "City of Trees" until 2017 when it was repainted with the words "America's Farm-to-Fork Capital" (referring to the [farm-to-fork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farm-to-fork "Farm-to-fork") movement, which promotes the consumption of locally-grown food). After 4,000 displeased citizens signed a petition protesting the change, officials agreed to include both slogans on the water tower.[\[35\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-36)

### Cityscape

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Cityscape")\]

#### City neighborhoods

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: City neighborhoods")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sacramento_%2C_California_%2833994662274%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_%2C_California_%2833994662274%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_,_California_(33994662274).jpg) [Downtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") is the home of numerous corporate regional headquarters.

The city used to group neighborhoods into four areas. As of 2011, the groupings were:

- Area One: [Alkali Flat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkali_Flat_Historic_District "Alkali Flat Historic District"), [Boulevard Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulevard_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Boulevard Park, Sacramento, California"), Campus Commons, [Sacramento State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"), Dos Rios Triangle, Downtown, East Sacramento, Mansion Flats, Marshall School, [Midtown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento"), [New Era Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Era_Park,_Sacramento,_California "New Era Park, Sacramento, California"), McKinley Village, [Newton Booth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#Newton_Booth_Historic_District), [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park"), [Poverty Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#Poverty_Ridge_Historic_District), Richards, Richmond Grove, River Park, Elmhurst, Sierra Oaks, [Southside Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southside_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Southside Park, Sacramento, California").[\[36\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-37)
- Area Two: Airport, Carleton Tract, Freeport Manor, Golf Course Terrace, [Greenhaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven,_Sacramento,_California "Pocket-Greenhaven, Sacramento, California") Hollywood Park, [Land Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Land Park, Sacramento, California"), Little Pocket, Mangan Park, [Meadowview](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meadowview,_Sacramento,_California "Meadowview, Sacramento, California"), Parkway, [Pocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven,_Sacramento,_California "Pocket-Greenhaven, Sacramento, California"), [Sacramento City College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_College "Sacramento City College"), [South Land Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_Park,_Sacramento,_California#South_Land_Park "Land Park, Sacramento, California"), Valley Hi / North Laguna, Z'Berg Park.[\[37\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-38)
- Area Three: Alhambra Triangle, Avondale, Brentwood, Carleton Tract, [Colonial Heights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Colonial Heights, Sacramento, California"), Colonial Manor, [Curtis Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curtis_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Curtis Park, Sacramento, California"), [Elmhurst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elmhurst,_Sacramento,_California "Elmhurst, Sacramento, California"), Fairgrounds, [Florin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florin,_California "Florin, California"), Fruitridge Manor, Glen Elder, Glenbrook, Granite Regional Park, Industrial Park, Lawrence Park, Med Center, North City Farms, [Oak Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oak_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Oak Park, Sacramento, California"), [Packard Bell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Packard_Bell "Packard Bell"), South City Farms, [Southeast Village](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Village "Southeast Village"), [Tahoe Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California#Tahoe_Park_East "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahoe_Park_South "Tahoe Park South"), Tallac Village, Vintage Park, Churchill Downs, and Woodbine.[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-39)
- Area Four: [Ben Ali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Ali,_Sacramento,_California "Ben Ali, Sacramento, California"), [Del Paso Heights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Del_Paso_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Del Paso Heights, Sacramento, California"), Gardenland, Hagginwood, McClellan Heights West, [Natomas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natomas,_Sacramento,_California "Natomas, Sacramento, California") (north, south, west), [North Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Sacramento "North Sacramento"), Northgate, [Robla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robla,_Sacramento,_California "Robla, Sacramento, California"), Swanston Estates, Terrace Manor, [Valley View Acres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valley_View_Acres,_Sacramento,_California "Valley View Acres, Sacramento, California"), and Woodlake.[\[39\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-40)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg) [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento") and [Downtown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") are seen from the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River").

Other neighborhoods in the city include Cal Expo, Capital Avenue, College/Glen, Creekside, Elder Creek, Erikson Industrial Park, Gateway Center, Gateway West, Glenwood Meadows, Hansen Park, Heritage Park, Johnson Business Park, Johnson Heights, Metro Center, Natomas Corporate Center, Natomas Creek, Natomas Crossing, Natomas Park, Newton Booth, Noralto, Northpointe, Norwood, Oak Knoll, Old North Sacramento, Parker Homes, Point West, Raley Industrial Park, Regency Park, Richardson Village, Richmond Grove, Sierra Oaks, Sports Complex, Strawberry Manor, Sundance Lake, Upper Land Park, Village 5, Village 7, Village 12, Village 14, Village Green, West Del Paso Heights, Westlake, Willowcreek, Wills Acres, Winn Park, and Youngs Heights.[\[40\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-41)

#### Notable areas

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Notable areas")\]

##### Capitol Mall

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Capitol Mall")\]

Capitol Mall connects West Sacramento and Downtown Sacramento. Some notable landmarks on this road include the Tower Bridge, Old Sacramento, and the California State Capitol Building. Capitol Mall is considered to be the business district of the city. Skyscrapers such as the [Wells Fargo Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Center_(Sacramento) "Wells Fargo Center (Sacramento)") and [U.S. Bank Tower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Sacramento) "U.S. Bank Tower (Sacramento)"), two of the tallest buildings in the city, are located on Capitol Mall and are home to several major companies. The street is also home to major festivals such as the annual Farm to Fork Festival.

Sacramento's historic [Japantown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japantown#United_States "Japantown") once occupied much of today's Capitol Mall, spanning 4th street from K to P streets. The area suffered from the forced [eviction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") of its Japanese residents during WW2 and never recovered, resulting in the remaining properties taken through eminent domain to create the grand promenade of today's [Capitol Mall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitol_Mall#History "Capitol Mall"). The [Nisei Memorial Hall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nisei_VFW_Post_8985 "Nisei VFW Post 8985") at 4th and Q remains the last remaining property associated with Sacramento's former Japantown.[\[41\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-42)

##### Downtown Commons

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Downtown Commons")\]

One of the newest districts in the city is [Downtown Commons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Commons "Downtown Commons"). Formerly home to the Downtown Plaza shopping mall, the district opened in 2016 along with [Golden 1 Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_1_Center "Golden 1 Center"). Downtown Commons, otherwise known as DOCO, is home to the Sawyer, a 16-story skyscraper with a 250-room hotel and 45 condominiums, a Macy's anchor store, an IMAX theater, and retail space with a variety of restaurants and shops.[\[42\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-43)

##### Downtown Sacramento

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Downtown Sacramento")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg/250px-Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg) Aerial view of Sacramento, clearly showing the downtown/midtown grid and surrounding areas

See also: [Downtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

Downtown Sacramento is home to the [SAFE Credit Union Convention Center and Theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex"), Sacramento City Hall, the [Sacramento Public Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Public_Library "Sacramento Public Library"), and [K Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K_Street_(Sacramento) "K Street (Sacramento)"), a historic street home to apartments, retail, and historical buildings. In addition, Downtown Sacramento is home to several hotels including the Citizen Hotel, housed in one of the first skyscrapers built in the city.[\[43\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-44)

##### East Sacramento

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: East Sacramento")\]

See also: [East Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Sacramento "East Sacramento")

East Sacramento is a neighborhood in between Midtown and Sacramento State. This neighborhood is well known for being home to McKinley Park and Rose Garden and the Fabulous Forties, home to some of the most expensive, largest, and architecturally unique homes in the city. East Sacramento was home to [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") during his term as Governor of California and this neighborhood was prominently featured in Greta Gerwig's film [Lady Bird](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lady_Bird_(film) "Lady Bird (film)").[\[44\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-45)

##### Historic Chinatown

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Historic Chinatown")\]

The [Opium Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opium_Wars "Opium Wars") of the 1840s and 1850s, along with the California gold rush, brought many Chinese people to California. Most arrived at San Francisco, which was then the largest city in California and known as "Daai Fau" ( [Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_language "Chinese language"): 大埠; [Jyutping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jyutping "Jyutping"): _daai6 fau6_; [Cantonese Yale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese "Yale romanization of Cantonese"): _Daaihfauh_). Some eventually came to Sacramento, then the second-largest city in California and consequently called "Yee Fow" (Chinese: 二埠; Jyutping: _ji6 fau6_). Today the city is known as "萨克拉门托" ( [pinyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): _Sàkèlāméntuō_) by mainland Chinese and as "沙加緬度" _Sāgāmíhndouh_ and _Shājiāmiǎnduó_ by Cantonese speakers and Taiwanese respectively.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg) Sacramento's historic Chinatown

Sacramento's [Chinatown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinatowns_in_the_United_States "Chinatowns in the United States") was on "I" Street from Second to Sixth Streets, called the [China Slough](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_Slough "China Slough"). At the time, this area of "I" Street was considered a health hazard because, lying within a levee zone, it was lower than other parts of the city, which were situated on higher land. Throughout Sacramento's Chinatown history, there were fires, acts of discrimination, and prejudicial legislation such as the [Chinese Exclusion Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Exclusion_Act "Chinese Exclusion Act") that was not repealed until 1943. The mysterious fires were thought to be set off by those who resented the Chinese working class.[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-46) Ordinances on what was viable building material were set into place to try to get the Chinese to move out. Newspapers such as [The Sacramento Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sacramento_Union "The Sacramento Union") wrote stories at the time that portrayed the Chinese in an unfavorable light to inspire ethnic discrimination and drive the Chinese away. While most of Sacramento's Chinatown has now been razed, a small Chinatown mall remains as well as a museum dedicated to the history of Sacramento's Chinatown.[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-47)[\[47\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-48)

##### Newton Booth Historic District

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Newton Booth Historic District")\]

The Newton Booth Historic District, named for [Newton Booth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton_Booth "Newton Booth"), is located on the southeast corner of Sacramento's original 1848 street grid.[\[48\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Newton-Booth-49)[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cityofsacramento-Historic-Register-074-50)[\[50\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-51)[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-sacbee-4484269-52)

##### Old Sacramento

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Old Sacramento")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_(cropped).jpg) The historic [Ebner's Hotel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebner%27s_Hotel "Ebner's Hotel"), built in 1856, in [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park")

The oldest part of the town besides [Sutter's Fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter%27s_Fort "Sutter's Fort") is [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park"), which consists of cobbled streets and many historic buildings, several from the 1850s and 1860s. Buildings have been preserved, restored, or reconstructed, and the district is now a substantial tourist attraction, with rides on steam-powered historic trains and horse-drawn carriages.

##### Lavender Heights

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Lavender Heights")\]

The Lavender District, formally designated as Lavender Heights in 2015, is central to Sacramento’s LGBTQ+ culture and community.[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-auto-53) It is home to the Gay & Lesbian Community Center, five LGBTQ+ nightclubs such as Badlands and [Faces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faces_(gay_club) "Faces (gay club)"), and numerous LGBTQ+-owned shops, galleries, and eateries.[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-auto-53)

##### Poverty Ridge Historic District

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Poverty Ridge Historic District")\]

The Poverty Ridge Historic District is within Sacramento's original 1848 street grid and bounded to the west by 21st Street, to the north by S Street, to the east by 23rd Street, to the south by W Street and U.S. Route 50, and includes the block bounded by 20th Street, 21st Street, S Street, and T Street.[\[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Poverty-Ridge-54)[\[54\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-newtonbooth-poverty-ridge-55)[\[55\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-56)

The Poverty Ridge Historic District was considered to be Sacramento's wealthiest
neighborhood from 1868 to 1947.[\[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Poverty-Ridge-54)[\[56\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cityofsacramento-Historic-Register-076-57)

### Climate

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Climate")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/American_River_at_Sunrise_Park%2C_June_1974_%2826251615404%29.jpg/250px-American_River_at_Sunrise_Park%2C_June_1974_%2826251615404%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:American_River_at_Sunrise_Park,_June_1974_(26251615404).jpg) The [American River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River "American River") is popular for [kayaking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kayaking "Kayaking") and [recreational boating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_boating "Recreational boating").

Sacramento has a [hot-summer Mediterranean climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate "Hot-summer Mediterranean climate") ( [Köppen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") _Csa_), characterized by long, hot, dry summers and short, mild, rainy winters. Most of the annual precipitation generally occurs from November to April, though there may be a day or two of light rainfall in May or October. The normal annual mean temperature is 61.8 °F (16.6 °C), with the monthly daily average temperature ranging from 47.3 °F (8.5 °C) in December to 75.9 °F (24.4 °C) in July.[\[57\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-NCEI_Summary_of_Monthly_Normals_-_Airport_-_1991-2020-58) Summer heat is sometimes moderated by a sea breeze known as the "delta breeze" which comes through the [Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento%E2%80%93San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta") from the [San Francisco Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay"), and temperatures cool down sharply at night.

The foggiest months are December and January. [Tule fog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tule_fog "Tule fog") can be extremely dense, lowering visibility to less than 100 feet (30 m) and making driving conditions extremely hazardous. Chilling tule fog events have been known to last for several consecutive days or weeks. During Tule fog events, temperatures do not exceed 50 °F (10 °C).

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg/250px-Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg) A [market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farmer%27s_market "Farmer's market") at César Chávez Plaza

Snowfall is rare in Sacramento, which is only 25 ft (8 m) [above sea level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level "Above mean sea level"). In the downtown area, only three significant snow accumulations have occurred since 1900, the last one being in 1976.[\[58\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-59) During especially cold winter and spring storms, intense showers do occasionally produce a significant amount of hail, which can create hazardous driving conditions. Snowfall in the city often melts upon ground contact, with traceable amounts occurring in some years. Significant annual snow accumulations occur in the foothills 40 mi (64 km) east of the city, which had brief and traceable amounts of snowfall in January 2002, December 2009, and February 2011.[\[59\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-60)[\[60\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-61) The greatest snowfall ever recorded in Sacramento was 3 inches (7.6 cm) on January 5, 1888.
On average, there are 76 days with a high of 90 °F (32 °C)+, and 14 days with a high of 100 °F (38 °C)+; On the other extreme, there are 8.5 days where the temperature remains below 50 °F (10 °C), and 15 freezing nights per year. Official temperature extremes range from 18 °F (−7.8 °C) on December 22, 1990, to 116 °F (46.7 °C) on September 6, 2022;[\[61\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-NOAA-62) a station around 5 mi (8.0 km) east-southeast of the city dipped to 17 °F (−8.3 °C) on December 11, 1932.[\[62\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-WRCC-63)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Sacramento_Skyline_%282%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Skyline_%282%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Skyline_(2)_(cropped).jpg) View of [Downtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

The average annual precipitation is 18.14 inches (461 mm). On average, precipitation falls on 58 days each year in Sacramento, and nearly all of this falls during the winter months. As in much of California, precipitation is highly variable from year to year, ranging from as little as 5.81 inches (148 mm) in 2013 to 33.44 inches (849 mm) in 1983.[\[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-64) Average January rainfall is 3.66 in (93 mm), and measurable precipitation is rare during the summer months. In February 1992, Sacramento had 16 consecutive days of rain, resulting in an accumulation of 6.41 in (163 mm) for the period. On rare occasions, monsoonal moisture surges from the Desert Southwest can bring upper-level moisture to the Sacramento region, leading to increased summer cloudiness, humidity, and even light showers and thunderstorms. Monsoon clouds do occur, usually during late June through early September. Sacramento is the second most flood-susceptible city in the United States after New Orleans.[\[64\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-65)

Sacramento has been noted as being the sunniest location on the planet for four months of the year, from June through September. It holds the distinction as the sunniest month, in terms of the percentage of possible sunshine, of anywhere in the world; July in Sacramento averages 14 hours and 12 minutes of sunshine per day, amounting to approximately 98% of possible sunshine.[\[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-66)

Since 2010, statewide [droughts in California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Droughts_in_California "Droughts in California") have further strained Sacramento's [water security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_security "Water security").[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-67)

Historical population

In 2002, the Civil Rights Project at Harvard University conducted for _Time_ magazine named Sacramento "America's Most Diverse City".[\[76\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-MostDiverseCity-TIME-78) The U.S. Census Bureau also groups Sacramento with other U.S. cities having a "high diversity" rating of the [diversity index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diversity_index "Diversity index").[\[77\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-79) Moreover, Sacramento is one of the most well-integrated U.S. cities, having a relatively high level of ethnic and racial heterogeneity within its neighborhoods.[\[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-80)

Chinese people are the largest Asian ethnic group in Sacramento, followed by Filipino, Indian, Vietnamese, Hmong and Japanese.[\[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-81)[\[80\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-82) Sacramento has the largest [Fijian American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fijian_American "Fijian American") community, including [Indo-Fijians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Fijian "Indo-Fijian").[\[81\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-83)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/CathBSlow_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-CathBSlow_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CathBSlow_(cropped).jpg) [Cathedral of the Blessed Sacrament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Blessed_Sacrament_in_Sacramento "Cathedral of the Blessed Sacrament in Sacramento"), the seat of the [Diocese of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Sacramento "Roman Catholic Diocese of Sacramento")

Sacramento, California – Racial and ethnic composition

_Note: the US Census treats Hispanic/Latino as an ethnic category. This table excludes Latinos from the racial categories and assigns them to a separate category. Hispanics/Latinos may be of any race._

### 2020

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: 2020")\]

The [2020 United States census](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_census "2020 United States census") reported that Sacramento had a population of 524,943. The population density was 5,323.4 inhabitants per square mile (2,055.4/km2). The racial makeup of Sacramento was 34.8% [White](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Americans "White Americans"), 13.2% [African American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Americans "African Americans"), 1.4% [Native American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States"), 19.9% [Asian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asian_Americans "Asian Americans"), 1.6% [Pacific Islander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Islander_Americans "Pacific Islander Americans"), 15.3% from [other races](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census) "Race (United States Census)"), and 13.8% from two or more races. [Hispanic or Latino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans "Hispanic and Latino Americans") of any race were 28.8% of the population.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-DP1-90)

The census reported that 96.7% of the population lived in households, 2.4% lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 0.9% were institutionalized.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-DP1-90)

There were 192,560 households, out of which 30.7% included children under the age of 18, 37.9% were married-couple households, 8.9% were [cohabiting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cohabitation "Cohabitation") couple households, 32.0% had a female householder with no partner present, and 21.2% had a male householder with no partner present. 29.5% of households were one person, and 10.3% were one person aged 65 or older. The average household size was 2.64.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-DP1-90) There were 116,436 [families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census) "Family (U.S. Census)") (60.5% of all households).[\[88\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-91)

The age distribution was 22.3% under the age of 18, 9.7% aged 18 to 24, 31.5% aged 25 to 44, 22.8% aged 45 to 64, and 13.8% who were 65years of age or older. The median age was 35.4years. For every 100 females, there were 95.2 males.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-DP1-90)

There were 202,231 housing units at an average density of 2,050.8 units per square mile (791.8 units/km2), of which 192,560 (95.2%) were occupied. Of these, 49.2% were owner-occupied, and 50.8% were occupied by renters.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-DP1-90)

In 2023, the US Census Bureau estimated that the median household income was $83,753, and the [per capita income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Per_capita_income "Per capita income") was $42,300. About 10.3% of families and 14.4% of the population were below the poverty line.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-92)

### 2010

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: 2010")\]

The [2010 United States census](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_census "2010 United States census")[\[90\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-census2010-93) reported Sacramento had a population of 466,488. The population density was 4,660.0 inhabitants per square mile (1,799.2/km2).

There were 138,165 Hispanic or Latino residents of any race (26.9%); 22.6% of

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_%285559878519%29.png/250px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_%285559878519%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_(5559878519).png) Map of racial distribution in [Greater Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Sacramento "Greater Sacramento"), 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people: **White**, **Black**, **Asian**, **Hispanic**, or **other**

the population was of Mexican heritage, 0.7% Puerto Rican, 0.5% Salvadoran, 0.2% Guatemalan, and 0.2% Nicaraguan.[\[91\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-94) [Non-Hispanic Whites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites "Non-Hispanic Whites") were 34.5% of the population in 2010,[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-census2-84) down from 71.4% in 1970.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-census1-85)

The census reported 458,174 people (98.2% of the population) lived in households, 4,268 (0.9%) lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 4,046 (0.9%) were institutionalized. Demographics were not affected by the end of the [2000s United States housing bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000s_United_States_housing_bubble "2000s United States housing bubble") and the [2008 financial crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_financial_crisis "2008 financial crisis").[\[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-95)[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-96)

There were 174,624 households, out of which 57,870 (33.1%) had children under the age of 18 living in them, 65,556 (37.5%) were [opposite-sex married couples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage "Marriage") living together, 27,640 (15.8%) had a female householder with no husband present, 10,534 (6.0%) had a male householder with no wife present. There were 13,234 (7.6%) [unmarried opposite-sex partnerships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSSLQ "POSSLQ"), and 2,498 (1.4%) [same-sex married couples or partnerships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_partnership_in_California "Domestic partnership in California"). 53,342 households (30.5%) were made up of individuals, and 14,926 (8.5%) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.62. There were 103,730 [families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census) "Family (U.S. Census)") (59.4% of all households); the average family size was 3.37.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sacramento%2C_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento%2C_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento,_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_(cropped).jpg) [Westminster Presbyterian Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_(Sacramento,_California) "Westminster Presbyterian Church (Sacramento, California)")

The age distribution of the city was as follows: 116,121 people (24.9%) were under the age of 18, 52,438 people (11.2%) aged 18 to 24, 139,093 people (29.8%) aged 25 to 44, 109,416 people (23.5%) aged 45 to 64, and 49,420 people (10.6%) who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33.0 years. For every 100 females, there were 94.9 males. For every 100 females aged 18 and over, there were 92.2 males.

There were 190,911 housing units at an average density of 1,907.1 units per square mile (736.3 units/km2), of which 86,271 (49.4%) were owner-occupied, and 88,353 (50.6%) were occupied by renters. The homeowner vacancy rate was 2.8%; the rental vacancy rate was 8.3%. 231,593 people (49.6% of the population) lived in owner-occupied housing units and 226,581 people (48.6%) lived in rental housing units.

Sacramento has one of the highest [LGBT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT "LGBT") populations per capita, ranking seventh among major American cities, and third in California, behind San Francisco and slightly behind Oakland, with roughly 10% of the city's total population identifying themselves as gay, lesbian, transgender, or bisexual.[\[94\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-The_Seattle_Times-97) [Lavender Heights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavender_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Lavender Heights, Sacramento, California") is a hub for LGBTQ activities in the city[\[95\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-98)[\[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-99) and is a centrally located district in [Midtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento") centered within and around K & 20th streets.

## Economy

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Economy")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Californiastatecapitol.jpg/250px-Californiastatecapitol.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Californiastatecapitol.jpg) The [California State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is the seat of the [Government of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California"), hosting the [Governor of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California") and the [California State Legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature").

The [Sacramento metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Sacramento metropolitan area") is the fifth largest in California after the [Los Angeles metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area "Los Angeles metropolitan area"), the [San Francisco Bay Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area"), the [Inland Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inland_Empire "Inland Empire"), and the [San Diego metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area "San Diego metropolitan area"), and is the [27th largest in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas "Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas"). [\[97\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-100)

Sacramento's economy has historically been dominated by the state and federal government and is currently home to more than 120,000 public sector employees. However, in recent years Sacramento has seen a diversification in its local economy, with gains being made in healthcare,[\[98\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-101) manufacturing,[\[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-102) and technology.[\[100\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-103) [Adventist Health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adventist_Health "Adventist Health"), [Aerojet Rocketdyne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerojet_Rocketdyne "Aerojet Rocketdyne"), [Blue Diamond Growers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Diamond_Growers "Blue Diamond Growers"), [Golden 1 Credit Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_1_Credit_Union "Golden 1 Credit Union"), [Kratos Defense & Security Solutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kratos_Defense_%26_Security_Solutions "Kratos Defense & Security Solutions"), [Nugget Markets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nugget_Markets "Nugget Markets"), Powerschool, [Raley's Supermarkets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raley%27s_Supermarkets "Raley's Supermarkets"), Solidigm, [Sutter Health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter_Health "Sutter Health"), Teichert, [The McClatchy Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company "The McClatchy Company"), and [VSP Vision Care](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VSP_Vision_Care "VSP Vision Care") are notable companies based in Sacramento and the surrounding metropolitan area. Other major companies that have operations in Sacramento include [Amazon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_(company) "Amazon (company)"),[\[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-104) [Apple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc "Apple Inc"), [Centene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centene "Centene"), [Hewlett-Packard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hewlett-Packard "Hewlett-Packard"), [Intel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intel "Intel"), [Oracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oracle_Corporation "Oracle Corporation"), and [Siemens Mobility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siemens_Mobility "Siemens Mobility").[\[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-105)[\[103\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-106)[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-107)

The [Port of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Sacramento "Port of Sacramento") has been plagued with operating losses in recent years and faces bankruptcy. This severe loss in business is due to the heavy competition from the [Port of Stockton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Stockton "Port of Stockton"), which has a larger facility and a deeper channel. As of 2006, the city of [West Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California") took responsibility for the Port of Sacramento. During the [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War") era, the Port of Sacramento was the major terminus in the supply route for all military parts, hardware, and other cargo going to Southeast Asia.
