## Culture

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Culture")\]

### Museums

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Museums")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crocker_Museum_entrance_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Crocker_Museum_entrance_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Crocker_Museum_entrance_(cropped).jpg) The [Crocker Art Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocker_Art_Museum "Crocker Art Museum") is the oldest public [art museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_museum "Art museum") in the [Western United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States") and has one of the largest public art collections in the country.

Sacramento is home to 32 museums, including several major museums. The [Crocker Art Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocker_Art_Museum "Crocker Art Museum") is the oldest public [art museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_museum "Art museum") west of the [Mississippi River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River"). In 2010, the museum completed an expansion that tripled the museum's floor space to more than 145,000 square feet of exhibit space.

Also of interest is the [Governor's Mansion State Historic Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor%27s_Mansion_State_Historic_Park "Governor's Mansion State Historic Park"), a large Victorian Mansion that was home to 14 of California's Governors. The [Leland Stanford Mansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leland_Stanford_Mansion "Leland Stanford Mansion"), which was completely restored in 2006, serves as the State's official address for diplomatic and business receptions. Guided public tours are available. [The California Museum for History, Women, and the Arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_California_Museum_for_History,_Women,_and_the_Arts "The California Museum for History, Women, and the Arts"), home of the [California Hall of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Hall_of_Fame "California Hall of Fame"), is a cultural destination. The [California State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is home to the [California State Capitol Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol_Museum "California State Capitol Museum") and offers free tours of the capitol's historic chambers and assembly rooms as well as a museum that is home to several historical artifacts.[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-109)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/California_Museum.jpg/250px-California_Museum.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:California_Museum.jpg) [The California Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_California_Museum "The California Museum") is dedicated to the [history of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_California "History of California") and also hosts the [California Hall of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Hall_of_Fame "California Hall of Fame").

The [California State Railroad Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Railroad_Museum "California State Railroad Museum") in Old Sacramento has historical exhibits and live steam locomotives that patrons may ride. The [California Automobile Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Automobile_Museum "California Automobile Museum"), just south of Old Sacramento, displays the automotive history and vehicles from 1880 to 2006 and is the oldest non-profit automotive museum in the West. [McClellan Air Force Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base "McClellan Air Force Base") is home to the [Aerospace Museum of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerospace_Museum_of_California "Aerospace Museum of California") where more than 40 civilian and military aircraft and 50 historical jet engines are displayed to the public. In addition, the [Sacramento History Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_History_Museum "Sacramento History Museum"), in the heart of Old Sacramento, focuses on the history of Sacramento from the region's pre-gold rush history through the present day. In 2021, the Museum of Science and Curiosity (MOSAC) opened in the restored historic power station building of Matsui Waterfront Park.

There is a Museum Day held in Sacramento every year when 26 museums in the greater Sacramento area offer free admission. The 2009 Sacramento Museum Day brought out more than 80,000 people, the largest number the event has gathered. Sacramento Museum Day is held every year on the first Saturday of February.

### Performing arts

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Performing arts")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg) [Sacramento Memorial Auditorium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex") hosts the [Sacramento Ballet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Ballet "Sacramento Ballet") and the [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra").

The [Sacramento Ballet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Ballet "Sacramento Ballet"), [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra"), and the Sacramento Opera perform at the SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center (formerly known as the Community Center Theater).

There are several major theater venues in Sacramento. The [Sacramento Convention Center Complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex") governs both the SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center and [Memorial Auditorium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memorial_Auditorium_(Sacramento) "Memorial Auditorium (Sacramento)"). The H Street Theatre Complex consists of the [Wells Fargo Pavilion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion"), built in 2003 atop the old Music Circus tent foundations, the McClatchy Mainstage, and the Pollock Stage, originally built as a television studio and renovated at the same time the Pavilion was built. These smaller venues seat 300 and 90, offering a more intimate presentation than the 2300-seat Pavilion. The [Eagle Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eagle_Theatre_(Sacramento,_California) "Eagle Theatre (Sacramento, California)") in Old Sacramento is a reconstruction of the oldest permanent theater in California and hosts several performances year-round.[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-110) The newest venue in the city, the Sophia Tsakopoulos Center for the Arts, consists of the 365-seat Sutter Theatre for Children and the Mainstage, seating 250.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg/250px-Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg) The [Wells Fargo Pavilion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion") hosts the [California Musical Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Musical_Theatre "California Musical Theatre") and the [Sacramento Theatre Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Theatre_Company "Sacramento Theatre Company").

Professional theatre is represented in Sacramento by several companies. [Broadway Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadway_Sacramento "Broadway Sacramento") and its locally produced [summer stock theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer_stock_theatre "Summer stock theatre"), [Broadway at Music Circus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadway_at_Music_Circus "Broadway at Music Circus"), lures many directors, performers, and artists from New York and Los Angeles to work alongside a large local staff at the [Wells Fargo Pavilion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion"). During the fall, winter, and spring seasons Broadway Sacramento brings bus and truck tours to the [SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAFE_Credit_Union_Performing_Arts_Center "SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center"). Resident at the H Street Theatre Complex for the remainder of the year (from September to May), the [Sacramento Theatre Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Theatre_Company "Sacramento Theatre Company") prepares to celebrate its 75th season, beginning in the Fall of 2019. In addition to a traditional regional theatre fare of classical plays and musicals, the Sacramento Theatre Company has a large School of the Arts with a variety of opportunities for arts education. The [B Street Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B_Street_Theatre "B Street Theatre"), having completed its 2018 move into the new Sofia Tsakopoulos Center for the Arts, continues its pursuit of producing smaller and more intimate professional works for families and children. Rounding out the professional companies is Capital Stage, which performed aboard the Delta King until the end of the 2010–2011 season and soon took up residence at its venue along the J-Street corridor.

The Sacramento area has one of the largest collections of community theatres in California. Some of these include the Thistle Dew Dessert Theatre and Playwrights Workshop, Davis Musical Theatre Co., El Dorado Musical Theatre, Runaway Stage Productions, River City Theatre Company, Flying Monkey Productions, The Actor's Theatre, KOLT Run Productions, Kookaburra Productions, Big Idea Theatre, Celebration Arts, Lambda Player, Light Opera Theatre of Sacramento, Synergy Stage and the historic Eagle Theatre. The [Sacramento Shakespeare Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Shakespeare_Festival "Sacramento Shakespeare Festival") provides entertainment under the stars every summer in William Land Park. Many of these theatres compete annually for the Elly Awards overseen by The Sacramento Area Regional Theatre Alliance or SARTA.[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-111)

### Visual arts

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Visual arts")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento%2C_California.jpg/250px-Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento%2C_California.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento,_California.jpg) The [Spanish Colonial Revival style](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_Revival_style "Spanish Colonial Revival style") Ramona Building, built in 1930

The Sacramento Metropolitan Arts Commission is an organization that was established as the Sacramento [arts council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arts_council "Arts council") in 1977 to provide several arts programs for the city. These include Art in Public Places, Arts Education, Grants, and Cultural Programs, Poet Laureate Programs, Arts Stabilization Programs and Other Resources, and opportunities.

Sacramento Second Saturday Art Walk is a program of local art galleries that stay open into the late evenings every second Saturday of each month.

Sacramento is also home to the [Wide Open Walls Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wide_Open_Walls_(Sacramento_Mural_Festival) "Wide Open Walls (Sacramento Mural Festival)") where artists from across the world have added more than 140 murals across the city since the festival's inception in 2016.[\[109\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-112)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG/250px-Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG) The [Sacramento Masonic Temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Masonic_Temple "Sacramento Masonic Temple")

Sacramento is home to one of California's oldest Latino cultural centers, the Latino Center of Art and Culture The Latino Center of Art and Culture was founded in the early '70s by activist Chicano students to combat racism and instill pride in the Chicano community. Known as La Raza Galeria it was home to artists like Ricardo Favela, José Montoya, and Esteban Villa who formed the Chicano artist collective, the Royal Chicano Air Force. The center is a community hub offering support to emerging Latino artists and producing live programming.[\[110\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-113)

### Music

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Music")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tower_Theater_%2850216124686%29.jpg/250px-Tower_Theater_%2850216124686%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tower_Theater_(50216124686).jpg) The Tower Theatre, where [Tower Records](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_Records "Tower Records") was founded

[Tower Records](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_Records_(music_retailer) "Tower Records (music retailer)") was started and based in Sacramento until its closing.[\[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-CHanksBornRaised-Playmaker-114) Classical music is widely available. The [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra"), the Sacramento Baroque Soloists, the Sacramento Choral Society & Orchestra, the [Sacramento Youth Symphony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Youth_Symphony "Sacramento Youth Symphony"), the Sacramento Master Singers, the Sacramento Children's Chorus, and the Camellia Symphony each present a full season of concerts.

Each year, the city hosts the Sammies, the Sacramento Music Awards. Sacramento also has a reputation\[ _[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_\] as a center for [Dixieland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dixieland "Dixieland") jazz, because of the [Sacramento Jazz Jubilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Jazz_Jubilee "Sacramento Jazz Jubilee") which was held every [Memorial Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memorial_Day "Memorial Day") weekend until 2017. Events and performances are held in multiple locations throughout the city. Each year thousands of jazz fans from all over the world visit for this one weekend.

A growing number of rock, [hardcore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardcore_punk "Hardcore punk"), and [metal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavy_metal_music "Heavy metal music") bands hail from the Sacramento area, including [Tesla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_(band) "Tesla (band)"), AS IS, [Deftones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deftones "Deftones"), [Papa Roach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papa_Roach "Papa Roach"), [Will Haven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Will_Haven "Will Haven"), [Trash Talk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trash_Talk_(band) "Trash Talk (band)"),[\[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-115)[\[113\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-116)[\[114\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-117) [Dance Gavin Dance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance_Gavin_Dance "Dance Gavin Dance"), [A Lot Like Birds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Lot_Like_Birds "A Lot Like Birds"), [Far](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_(band) "Far (band)"), [CAKE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cake_(band) "Cake (band)"), [!!!](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/!!! "!!!"), [Oleander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oleander_(band) "Oleander (band)") and [Steel Breeze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steel_Breeze "Steel Breeze"); plus some other famous musicians like record producer and recording artist [Charlie Peacock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Peacock "Charlie Peacock"), Duane Leinan, Bob Stubbs of [Social Distortion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Distortion "Social Distortion"), and Craig Chaquico of [Jefferson Starship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jefferson_Starship "Jefferson Starship").

Sacramento is home to several music festivals throughout the year. Since 2012, Sacramento hosts the four-day [Aftershock Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftershock_Festival "Aftershock Festival") at [Discovery Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discovery_Park_(Sacramento) "Discovery Park (Sacramento)") where acclaimed bands such as [Evanescence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evanescence "Evanescence"), [Kiss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiss_(band) "Kiss (band)"), and [Muse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muse_(band) "Muse (band)") perform for up to 160,000 visitors. Other notable music festivals include the country-based GoldenSky Festival and the soul and R&B-based [Sol Blume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sol_Blume "Sol Blume") festival.[\[115\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-118)[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-119)

Scottish pop band [Middle of the Road](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_of_the_Road_(band) "Middle of the Road (band)") sang kindly of Sacramento in their 1972 European hit song " [Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_(A_Wonderful_Town) "Sacramento (A Wonderful Town)")". [Experimental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Experimental_music "Experimental music") groups such as [Hella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hella_(band) "Hella (band)"), [Death Grips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_Grips "Death Grips"), and [Tera Melos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tera_Melos "Tera Melos") also come out of Sacramento.

Rappers [C-Bo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-Bo "C-Bo"), [Marvaless](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvaless "Marvaless"), [Lunasicc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunasicc "Lunasicc"), [Mozzy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozzy "Mozzy"), [Hobo Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hobo_Johnson "Hobo Johnson"), and [Chuuwee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuuwee "Chuuwee") are among those native to the area.

### Film

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Film")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/K_Street%2C_Downtown_Sacramento%2C_California_%2851030469438%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-K_Street%2C_Downtown_Sacramento%2C_California_%2851030469438%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:K_Street,_Downtown_Sacramento,_California_(51030469438)_(cropped).jpg) The historic [Crest Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crest_Theatre "Crest Theatre")

Sacramento is home to the [Sacramento French Film Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_French_Film_Festival "Sacramento French Film Festival"), a cultural event held every year in July that features U.S. premieres of French films and classic masterpieces of French cinema, and the Sacramento Japanese Film Festival,[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-120) also held in July. In addition, Sacramento is home to the Trash Film Orgy, a summer film festival celebrating the absurd, B-movies, horror, monster, and exploitation films.[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-121) Founded in 2007, the Sacramento Horror Film Festival showcases feature-length and short films as well as live musical and theatrical performances in the horror and macabre genres.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-122)

Of note, Sacramento has been home to various actors, including [Eddie Murphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddie_Murphy "Eddie Murphy"), who resided in the Riverlake community of [Pocket-Greenhaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven "Pocket-Greenhaven") with his then-wife Nicole Mitchell Murphy, a fashion model and Sacramento native. It is also the home of director [Greta Gerwig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greta_Gerwig "Greta Gerwig"), whose solo directorial debut [_Lady Bird_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lady_Bird_(film) "Lady Bird (film)") is set in Sacramento.

### Cuisine

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Cuisine")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/The_Old_Tavern_%28Sacramento%2C_CA%29.jpg/250px-The_Old_Tavern_%28Sacramento%2C_CA%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Old_Tavern_(Sacramento,_CA).jpg) The [Old Tavern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Tavern_(Sacramento,_California) "Old Tavern (Sacramento, California)"), built in the 1850s

In 2012, Sacramento started the marketing campaign as "America's Farm-to-Fork Capital" due to Sacramento's many restaurants that source their food from the numerous surrounding farms[\[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-123) as well as the region's many certified farmers' markets.[\[121\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-124) Several notable farmers' market operate in the City of Sacramento, including:

- [Central Sacramento Sunday Certified Farmers' Market](https://alchemistcdc.org/central/) \- one of the largest and longest-running agriculture-focused certified farmers' markets in California, it takes place every Sunday morning under the freeway overpass, across from [Southside Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southside_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Southside Park, Sacramento, California")[\[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-125)
- [Midtown Farmers' Market](https://exploremidtown.org/midtown-markets/) \- a large Saturday morning farmers' market that includes many hot food, packaged food, and craft vendors, the Midtown Farmers' Market was voted the #1 farmers' market in California and #3 farmers' market in the United States in 2025[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-126)
- [Florin Certified Farmers' Market](https://alchemistcdc.org/florin/) \- located at the [Florin Light Rail Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florin_station "Florin station") year-round on Thursday mornings, the Florin Certified Farmers' Market is among the top farmers' markets in the United States for [EBT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supplemental_Nutrition_Assistance_Program "Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program") usage.[\[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-127)

The city has an annual Farm-to-Fork festival that showcases various grocers, restaurants, and growers in the industry, and is the current host city for [Terra Madre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terra_Madre_Salone_del_Gusto "Terra Madre Salone del Gusto") Americas.[\[125\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-128) In 2012, one of the city's farm-to-fork restaurants [The Kitchen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Kitchen_(California_restaurant) "The Kitchen (California restaurant)") was nominated for Outstanding Restaurant by the James Beard Foundation.[\[126\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-129) Sacramento is home to well-known cookbook authors, [Biba Caggiano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biba_Caggiano "Biba Caggiano") of Biba's Restaurant and Mai Pham of Lemongrass and Star Ginger.[\[127\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-130)

Sacramento is also known for its alcoholic beverage culture, with keystone events that include [Cal Expo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cal_Expo "Cal Expo")'s Grape and Gourmet, Sacramento Beer Week, and Sacramento Cocktail Week. Its growing beer scene is evident, with over 60 microbreweries in the region as of 2017.[\[128\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-131) Numerous beer festivals around the region highlight both local and visitor beers. In addition to festivals in Elk Grove,[\[129\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-132) Davis, Roseville, Placerville,[\[130\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-133) and Woodland,[\[131\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-134) Sacramento hosts the annual California Beer Craft Summit, an exposition dedicated to the art of brewing. The summit also hosts the largest beer festival on the West Coast, featuring over 160 breweries in downtown Sacramento.[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-135)

Sacramento's contemporary culture is also reflected in its coffee. An "underrated coffee city",[\[133\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-136) Sacramento has above-average marks for local coffee.[\[134\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-137)

## Sports

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Sports")\]

Main article: [Sports in Sacramento, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_in_Sacramento,_California "Sports in Sacramento, California")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/G1C_Interior.jpg/250px-G1C_Interior.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:G1C_Interior.jpg) A [Sacramento Kings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings") game at [Golden 1 Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_1_Center "Golden 1 Center") in [Downtown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

Sacramento is home of the [Sacramento Kings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings") of the [National Basketball Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association"). The Kings came to Sacramento from Kansas City in 1985. On January 21, 2013, a controlling interest in the Sacramento Kings was sold to hedge fund manager [Chris Hansen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_R._Hansen "Chris R. Hansen"), who intended to move the franchise to Seattle for the 2013–2014 NBA season and rename the team the [Seattle SuperSonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle_SuperSonics "Seattle SuperSonics").[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-138) Sacramento Mayor [Kevin Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Johnson_(basketball_player) "Kevin Johnson (basketball player)"), himself a former NBA basketball player, fought the move, forming an ownership group led by [Vivek Ranadive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vivek_Ranadive "Vivek Ranadive") to keep the Kings in Sacramento. On May 16, 2013, the NBA Board of Governors voted 22–8 to keep the Kings in Sacramento.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-139)

[Sacramento Republic FC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Republic_FC "Sacramento Republic FC") of [USL Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USL_Championship "USL Championship") began play to in April 2014 at [Hughes Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_C._Hughes_Stadium "Charles C. Hughes Stadium") before a sellout crowd of 20,231, setting a USL Pro regular-season single-game attendance record.[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-140)[\[138\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-141) They now play in Papa Murphy's Park. Republic FC won the [USL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Soccer_League "United Soccer League") championship in their first season. In October 2019, Republic FC's [Major League Soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Soccer "Major League Soccer") expansion bid was approved; the team was expected to begin MLS play in the 2022 season,[\[139\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-142) until being delayed by COVID-19 to the 2023 season.[\[140\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-143) However, as of February 26, 2021, the bid is on indefinite hiatus.[\[141\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-144)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG/250px-City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG) View from [Sutter Health Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter_Health_Park "Sutter Health Park"), home of the [Sacramento River Cats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River_Cats "Sacramento River Cats") and the temporary home of the [Athletics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athletics_(baseball) "Athletics (baseball)").

In 2000, AAA minor league baseball returned to Sacramento with the [Sacramento River Cats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River_Cats "Sacramento River Cats"), an affiliate of the [San Francisco Giants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants "San Francisco Giants") and formerly an affiliate of the [Oakland Athletics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oakland_Athletics "Oakland Athletics"). The River Cats play at [Sutter Health Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutter_Health_Park "Sutter Health Park"), in West Sacramento. The [Athletics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athletics_(baseball) "Athletics (baseball)") of [Major League Baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Baseball "Major League Baseball"), as part of their relocation from Oakland to [Las Vegas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Las_Vegas "Las Vegas"), will temporarily play at Sutter Health Park from 2025 to 2027 (with an option for 2028), until their new stadium in Las Vegas is completed.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-145)

The [Sacramento State Hornets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_State_Hornets_football "Sacramento State Hornets football") of the [NCAA Division I Football Championship Subdivision (FCS)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NCAA_Division_I "NCAA Division I") play at [Hornet Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hornet_Stadium_(Sacramento) "Hornet Stadium (Sacramento)") as part of the [Big Sky Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference "Big Sky Conference"). Since 1954, the Hornets have won seven conference titles and have participated in four playoff appearances and two bowl games.

Sacramento is the former home of two professional basketball teams. The [Sacramento Heatwave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Heatwave "Sacramento Heatwave") of the [American Basketball Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(21st_century) "American Basketball Association (21st century)") previously played in the Sacramento area until 2013. Sacramento was also formerly home to the now-defunct [Sacramento Monarchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Monarchs "Sacramento Monarchs") of the [WNBA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association "Women's National Basketball Association"). The Monarchs were one of the eight founding members of the WNBA in 1997 and won the [WNBA Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WNBA_Championship "WNBA Championship") in 2005, but folded in November 2009.

Sacramento has frequently hosted the [NCAA Men's Outdoor Track and Field Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Outdoor_Track_and_Field_Championship "NCAA Men's Outdoor Track and Field Championship") as well as the first and second rounds of the [NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship "NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship"). The California International Marathon (est. 1983) attracts a field of international elite runners who vie for a share of the $50,000 prize purse. The fast course is popular for runners seeking to achieve a Boston Marathon qualifying time and fitness runners.

## Parks and recreation

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Parks and recreation")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Capitol_Mall_Sacramento%2CCA.jpg/330px-Capitol_Mall_Sacramento%2CCA.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Capitol_Mall_Sacramento,CA.jpg) The [Capitol Mall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitol_Mall "Capitol Mall") is a major monumental [parkway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parkway "Parkway") leading from [Tower Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_Bridge_(Sacramento) "Tower Bridge (Sacramento)") to the [California Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol").

Sacramento boasts an extensive park system consisting of over 5,000 acres (2,023 ha) of parkland and recreation centers.[\[143\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-146) In its 2013 ParkScore ranking, [The Trust for Public Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trust_for_Public_Land "Trust for Public Land") reported Sacramento was tied with San Francisco and [Boston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston "Boston") for having the third-best park system among the 50 most populous U.S. cities.[\[144\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-147) ParkScore ranks city park systems by a formula that analyzes the city's median park size, park acres as percent of city area, the percent of residents within a half-mile of a park, spending of park services per resident, and the number of playgrounds per 10,000 residents.

The city features a collection of smaller parks in the downtown district, including Crocker Park, Roosevelt Park, Fremont Park, and Southside Park, and is home to basketball courts, playgrounds, and year-round farmers markets and local events. In addition, [Cesar Chavez Plaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cesar_Chavez_Plaza "Cesar Chavez Plaza") is home to concerts in the summertime and is a well-known rallying spot for gatherings. In addition, surrounding the [California State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is [Capitol Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitol_Park_(Sacramento) "Capitol Park (Sacramento)"), a 40 acres (16 ha) park consisting of more than 200 types of trees and 155 memorials. The most recent park constructed in Sacramento is the Hanami Line at [Robert Matsui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Matsui "Robert Matsui") Waterfront Park, which is home to a line of [Cherry Blossoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cherry_blossom "Cherry blossom") surrounding the park.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-148) Popular parks outside the central core include [American River Parkway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River_Parkway "American River Parkway") which spans 23 miles along the American River, William McKinley Park and Memorial Rose Garden, and [William Land Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Land_Park "William Land Park").

[William Land Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Land_Park "William Land Park") is home to several key attractions in the city. The [Sacramento Zoo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Zoo "Sacramento Zoo") spans 14.3 acres (5.8 ha) and is home to more than 400 native and endangered animals around the world. The park is also home to Funderland, a small amusement park open from February to November consisting of 9 rides, and Fairytale Town, which sees more than 250,000 visitors each year. Once a year a [fire dancing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fire_dancing "Fire dancing") exhibition known as The Fire Spectacular is held in the park amphitheater. Groups from across Sacramento come to compete for the title of "Obsidian Fire". Jim Souza, the lead organizer of the event, came under controversy after local [H.O.A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homeowner_association "Homeowner association") members reported hooded individuals wearing black fire emblems strolling around the park. He denied having any connections and announced the event is still planned for fall 2024 of this year.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-149)[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-150)[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-151)[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-152)

Sacramento is a hotbed for high school rugby. [Jesuit High School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesuit_High_School_(Sacramento) "Jesuit High School (Sacramento)") is the recent defending national champion (winning five times in total). Their arch-rival school Christian Brothers came in second nationwide. Burbank, Del Campo, and Vacaville have also placed well in the national competition over the years. The Sacramento Valley High School Rugby Conference hosts the largest and arguably deepest preseason youth and high school rugby tournament in America.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633011.tif/lossy-page1-250px-Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633011.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento,_California_LCCN2013633011.tif) The [California State Fair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Fair "California State Fair") is held annually at the [California Exposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Exposition "California Exposition").

The [California State Fair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Fair "California State Fair") is held in Sacramento each year at the end of the summer, ending on [Labor Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_Day "Labor Day"). In 2010, the State Fair moved to July. More than one million people attended this fair in 2001. The [Jedediah Smith Memorial Trail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jedediah_Smith_Memorial_Trail "Jedediah Smith Memorial Trail") that runs between [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento") and [Folsom Lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folsom_Lake "Folsom Lake") grants access to the American River Parkway, a natural area that includes more than 5,000 acres (20 km2) of undeveloped land. It attracts cyclists and equestrians from across the state. Among other recreational options in Sacramento is Discovery Park, a 275-acre (1.1 km2) park studded with stands of mature trees and grasslands. This park is situated where the American River flows into the Sacramento River.

Since 1991, Capitol Casino has been open in downtown Sacramento and is home to several card games. Other notable casinos in the area include [Thunder Valley Casino Resort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thunder_Valley_Casino_Resort "Thunder Valley Casino Resort"), [Cache Creek Casino Resort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cache_Creek_Casino_Resort "Cache Creek Casino Resort"), and Hard Rock Hotel & Casino Sacramento at Fire Mountain.

In amateur sports, Sacramento claims many prominent Olympians such as [Mark Spitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Spitz "Mark Spitz"), [Debbie Meyer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debbie_Meyer "Debbie Meyer") (6-time gold medalist in US swimming), [Mike Burton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Burton_(swimmer) "Mike Burton (swimmer)"), [Summer Sanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer_Sanders "Summer Sanders") (gold medalist in swimming, and trained in childhood by Debbie Meyer), [Jeff Float](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Float "Jeff Float") (all swimming), and [Billy Mills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Mills "Billy Mills") (track). Coach [Sherm Chavoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherm_Chavoor "Sherm Chavoor") founded Arden Hills Swim Club just east of the city and trained Burton, Spitz, and others.

## Government

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Government")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_(cropped).jpg) [Sacramento City Hall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_Hall "Sacramento City Hall") is the seat of the [Government of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento "Government of Sacramento"), hosting the [Mayor of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_Sacramento "Mayor of Sacramento") and [Sacramento City Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_Council "Sacramento City Council").

Sacramento is both the capital city of California and the [county seat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County_seat "County seat") of [Sacramento County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_County "Sacramento County"). As such, it hosts both the [Californian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California") and the county administration, alongside the city government.

### City government

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: City government")\]

Main article: [Government of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento "Government of Sacramento")

The [Government of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento,_California "Government of Sacramento, California") operates as a [charter city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charter_city "Charter city") (as opposed to a general law city) under the Charter of the City of Sacramento. The elected government is composed of the [Sacramento City Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_Council "Sacramento City Council") with 8 city council districts and the [Mayor of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayor_of_Sacramento "Mayor of Sacramento"), which operates under a [council-manager government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council-manager_government "Council-manager government"). In addition, there are numerous departments and appointed officers such as the City Manager, [Sacramento Police Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Police_Department "Sacramento Police Department") (SPD), the [Sacramento Fire Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Fire_Department "Sacramento Fire Department") (SFD), City Clerk, City Attorney, and City Treasurer.

The current mayor is [Kevin McCarty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McCarty "Kevin McCarty") and the council members are Lisa Kaplan, Roger Dickinson, Karina Talamantes, Phil Pluckebaum, Caity Maple, Eric Guerra, Rick Jennings, and [Mai Vang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mai_Vang "Mai Vang").[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-cc-4) The City of Sacramento is part of [Sacramento County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_County,_California "Sacramento County, California"), for which the [government of Sacramento County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento_County,_California "Government of Sacramento County, California") is defined and authorized under the [California Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Constitution "California Constitution"), [California law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_law "California law"), and the Charter of the County of Sacramento.[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-153)

### California government

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: California government")\]

Main article: [Government of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California")

As the [capital city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California"), Sacramento is home to the [government of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California"). The California State Capitol is the seat of the [governor of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California") and the [California State Legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature"), and the city is home to numerous [California state agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_California_state_agencies "List of California state agencies"). The [Supreme Court of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California "Supreme Court of California") is headquartered in San Francisco but maintains one of its two branch offices in Sacramento, where it shares a courtroom with the [Court of Appeal for the Third Appellate District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Courts_of_Appeal "California Courts of Appeal").

### State and federal representation

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: State and federal representation")\]

In the [California State Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Senate "California State Senate"), Sacramento is in the [8th Senate District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California%27s_8th_State_Senatorial_district "California's 8th State Senatorial district"). In the [California State Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Assembly "California State Assembly") it is in the [6th Assembly District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California%27s_6th_State_Assembly_district "California's 6th State Assembly district") and [10th Assembly District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California%27s_10th_State_Assembly_district "California's 10th State Assembly district").

In the [United States House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives"), Sacramento is split between two districts. The northern half is in [California's 6th congressional district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California%27s_6th_congressional_district "California's 6th congressional district"), represented by [Democrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") [Ami Bera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ami_Bera "Ami Bera").[\[151\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-154) The southern half is in [California's 7th congressional district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California%27s_7th_congressional_district "California's 7th congressional district"), represented by [Democrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") [Doris Matsui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doris_Matsui "Doris Matsui").

## Education

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Education")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_(cropped).jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/UCDMCaerial.jpg/250px-UCDMCaerial.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:UCDMCaerial.jpg)

The main campus of the [University of California, Davis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis "University of California, Davis"), is in [Davis, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davis,_California "Davis, California") (top), while the [UC Davis Medical Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") is in Sacramento (bottom).

### Higher education

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Higher education")\]

See also: [California State University, Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"); [University of California, Davis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis "University of California, Davis"); and [University of the Pacific (United States)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)")

The Sacramento area hosts a wide variety of higher educational opportunities. There are two major public universities, many private institutions, community colleges, vocational schools, and the McGeorge School of Law.

Sacramento is home to [Sacramento State (California State University, Sacramento)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"), founded as Sacramento State College in 1947. In 2004, enrollment was 22,555 undergraduates and 5,417 graduate students in the university's eight colleges. The university's mascot is the hornet, and the school colors are green and gold. The 300-acre (1.2 km2) campus is along the American River Parkway a few miles east of downtown.

The [University of California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California "University of California") has a campus, [UC Davis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis "UC Davis"), in nearby [Davis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davis,_California "Davis, California") and has a graduate center in downtown Sacramento. The [UC Davis Graduate School of Management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_School_of_Management "UC Davis Graduate School of Management") (GSM) is near the [UC Davis Medical Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") off Stockton Boulevard near Highway 50. Many students, about 400 out of 517, at the UC Davis GSM are working professionals and are completing their MBA part-time.[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-155) UC also maintains the University of California Sacramento Center (UCCS) for undergraduate and graduate studies.[\[153\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-156) The [UC Davis School of Medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Medicine "UC Davis School of Medicine") is at the [UC Davis Medical Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") between the neighborhoods of [Elmhurst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elmhurst,_Sacramento,_California "Elmhurst, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), and Oak Park.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg/250px-Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg) [Sacramento State University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento") is part of the [California State University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University "California State University") system.[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Drexel_University%2C_Sacramento_campus.JPG/250px-Drexel_University%2C_Sacramento_campus.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Drexel_University,_Sacramento_campus.JPG) [Former Drexel University Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drexel_University_Sacramento "Drexel University Sacramento")

The [Los Rios Community College District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Rios_Community_College_District "Los Rios Community College District") consists of several [two-year colleges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_college "Community college") in the Sacramento area— [American River College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River_College "American River College"), [Cosumnes River College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College "Cosumnes River College"), [Sacramento City College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_College "Sacramento City College"), and [Folsom Lake College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folsom_Lake_College "Folsom Lake College"), plus a large number of outreach centers for those colleges. [Sierra College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_College "Sierra College") is on the outskirts of Sacramento in Rocklin.

The [University of the Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)") has its Sacramento Campus in the Oak Park neighborhood of Sacramento. The campus has long included [McGeorge School of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McGeorge_School_of_Law "McGeorge School of Law") and in 2015 was expanded to become a comprehensive graduate and professional campus, including programs in analytics, business, education, health sciences, and public policy.[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-157) The [National University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_University_(California) "National University (California)") Sacramento regional campus offers bachelor's and master's degrees in business, education, health-care and teaching credential programs.

The [University of San Francisco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco "University of San Francisco") has one of its four regional campuses in Sacramento. At the undergraduate level, they offer degrees in Applied Economics, Information Systems, Organizational Behavior and Leadership, and Public Administration. At the graduate level, Master's programs are offered in Information Security and Assurance, Information Systems, Organization Development, Project Management, Public Administration, Nonprofit Administration, and Counseling.[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-158)

The private [University of Southern California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Southern_California "University of Southern California") has an extension in downtown Sacramento, called the State Capital Center. The campus, taught by main campus professors, Sacramento-based professors, and practitioners in the State Capitol and state agencies, offers Master of Public Administration, Masters of Public Policy, and Master of Public Health degrees.[\[156\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-159)

[Epic Bible College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_Bible_College "Epic Bible College") and the [Professional School of Psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_School_of_Psychology "Professional School of Psychology") are also based in Sacramento. [Western Seminary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Seminary "Western Seminary") has one of its four campuses in Sacramento, which opened on the campus of Arcade Church in 1991. Western is an evangelical, Christian graduate school that provides theological training for students who hope to serve in a variety of ministry roles including pastors, marriage and family therapists, educators, missionaries, and lay leadership. The Sacramento campus offers four master's degrees and a variety of other graduate-level programs.[\[157\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-160)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png/250px-McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png) The [McGeorge School of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McGeorge_School_of_Law "McGeorge School of Law") of the [University of the Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)") is a [law school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_school "Law school") in the [Oak Park neighborhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oak_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Oak Park, Sacramento, California").

A satellite campus of [Alliant International University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliant_International_University "Alliant International University") offers graduate and undergraduate programs of study.

[Carrington College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carrington_College_(US) "Carrington College (US)"), a for-profit institution, maintains a campus in Sacramento serving 2200 students. The school offers five programs in the healthcare professions.[\[158\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-161)

[The Art Institute of California – Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_California_%E2%80%93_Sacramento "The Art Institute of California – Sacramento") was established in 2007 and is a branch of [The Art Institute of California – Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_California_%E2%80%93_Los_Angeles "The Art Institute of California – Los Angeles"). The school is focused on educating students in the field of commercial arts. The school offers both a Bachelor of Science and an Associate of Science degree, as well as diplomas in some areas of study. Some majors the school offers are Digital Film-making & Video Production, Culinary Management, Graphic Design, and Game Art & Design. The school has since been closed.

On J Street, there is the [Lincoln Law School of Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lincoln_Law_School_of_Sacramento "Lincoln Law School of Sacramento"), a private, evening-only law school program with a strong legal presence in the region.

The [Universal Technical Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Technical_Institute "Universal Technical Institute") (UTI) is in Sacramento; it offers automotive programs in auto mechanics, auto body, and diesel.

### Primary and secondary education

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Primary and secondary education")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg/250px-C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg) The historic McClatchy High School[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_(cropped).jpg) Saint Patrick Academy[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_(cropped).jpg) North Sacramento School

The Sacramento area is served by various public school districts. They are: the [Sacramento City Unified School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_City_Unified_School_District "Sacramento City Unified School District"), [Natomas Unified School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natomas_Unified_School_District "Natomas Unified School District"), [San Juan Unified School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Juan_Unified_School_District "San Juan Unified School District"), [Twin Rivers Unified School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twin_Rivers_Unified_School_District "Twin Rivers Unified School District"), [Elk Grove Unified School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elk_Grove_Unified_School_District "Elk Grove Unified School District"), and [Robla Elementary School District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robla_Elementary_School_District "Robla Elementary School District"); secondary students in grades 7–12 in the Robla area are assigned to Twin Rivers USD.[\[159\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-SacCoSDMap2020-162) As of 2009, the area's schools employed 9,600 elementary school teachers (not including special education teachers),[\[160\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-163) and 7,410 middle school teachers (not including special education or vocational teachers).[\[161\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-164)

Almost all areas south of the American River are served by the Sacramento City Unified School District. The only exceptions are the Valley Hi/North Laguna and Florin areas served by the Elk Grove Unified School District.

Areas north of the American River are served by the remaining school districts. This area was not originally part of the City of Sacramento and as such is not served by Sacramento City Unified School District. North Sacramento outside of Natomas and Robla (for K-8) is served by the Twin Rivers Unified School District. The Robla area is served by the Robla School District for K-8 and by Twin Rivers for 9–12. The [Natomas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natomas,_Sacramento,_California "Natomas, Sacramento, California") region is served by the Natomas Unified School District. The Campus Commons area and the small portions of the Sierra Oaks neighborhood that fall into the city of Sacramento are served by the San Juan Unified School District.

While Roman Catholic institutions still dominate the independent school scene in the Sacramento area, in 1964, [Sacramento Country Day School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Country_Day_School "Sacramento Country Day School") opened and offered Sacramento citizens an independent school affiliated with the California Association of Independent Schools. SCDS has grown to its present-day status as a learning community for students from pre-kindergarten through twelfth grade. Additionally, the suburb of [Fair Oaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_Oaks,_California "Fair Oaks, California") hosts the expansive riverside campus of the [Sacramento Waldorf School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Waldorf_School "Sacramento Waldorf School"), a [Steiner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waldorf_Education "Waldorf Education") school adjacent to the Rudolf Steiner College, and the largest Waldorf school in North America. Sacramento Waldorf School educates students from pre-K through 12th grade on a secluded, pastoral site that incorporates a large, functioning [biodynamic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodynamic_agriculture "Biodynamic agriculture") farm.

Shalom School is the only Jewish day school in Sacramento; however, Brookefield School on property owned by Congregation B'nai Israel provides extracurricular Jewish education.

Capital Christian School is a preschool–12th grade private Christian school.[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-165) There is a small Bible college on campus offering associate degrees in Bible studies or theology. Sacramento Adventist Academy is another Christian school in Greater Sacramento. This is a preschool–12 institution, as well.

There is one Islamic school in Sacramento, Masjid Annur, founded in 1988.

The city also offers secular private schools, including [Merryhill School](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Merryhill_School&action=edit&redlink=1 "Merryhill School (page does not exist)") in Midtown.[\[163\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-166)[\[164\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-167)

### Public libraries

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Public libraries")\]

The [Sacramento Public Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Public_Library "Sacramento Public Library") system has 28 branches in the greater area.
