## Transportation

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Transportation")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_%2833055244176%29.jpg/250px-The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_%2833055244176%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_(33055244176).jpg) [Tower Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_Bridge_(Sacramento) "Tower Bridge (Sacramento)") crosses over the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River"), connecting Sacramento to [West Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California").

Main article: [Transportation in the Sacramento metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_in_the_Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Transportation in the Sacramento metropolitan area")

A 2021 study by [Walk Score](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walk_Score "Walk Score") ranked Sacramento the 49th most walkable of the 130 largest U.S. cities.[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-168)

### Roads

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Roads")\]

Sacramento is a [control city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_city "Control city") and the region is served by several highways and freeways. [Interstate 80](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_80_(California) "Interstate 80 (California)") (I-80) is the major east–west route, connecting Sacramento with San Francisco in the west, and [Reno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reno,_Nevada "Reno, Nevada") in the east. [Business 80](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_80_Business_(Sacramento,_California) "Interstate 80 Business (Sacramento, California)") (the Capital City Freeway) splits from I-80 in [West Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California"), runs through Sacramento, and then rejoins its parent in the northwest portion of the city. [U.S. Highway 50](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Route_50_(California) "U.S. Route 50 (California)") also begins its eastern journey in West Sacramento, [co-signed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concurrency_(road) "Concurrency (road)") with Business 80, but then splits off and heads toward [South Lake Tahoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Lake_Tahoe,_California "South Lake Tahoe, California") as the El Dorado Freeway. A sign at the eastern terminus of US 50 in [Ocean City, Maryland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean_City,_Maryland "Ocean City, Maryland"), gives the distance to Sacramento as 3,073 miles (4,946 km).[\[166\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-169)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Guy_West_Bridge_%285248634716%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Guy_West_Bridge_%285248634716%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Guy_West_Bridge_(5248634716)_(cropped).jpg) [Guy West Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_West_Bridge "Guy West Bridge") is a pedestrian and cyclist crossing over the [American River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River "American River"), connecting [California State University, Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento") to the Campus Commons neighborhood.

[Interstate 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_5_(California) "Interstate 5 (California)") (I-5) runs through Sacramento, heads north up to [Redding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redding,_California "Redding, California"), and then heads south near the western edge of the [California Central Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Central_Valley "California Central Valley") towards Los Angeles. [California State Highway 99](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Route_99 "California State Route 99") runs through Sacramento, heading closer to the eastern edge of the Central Valley, connecting to [Marysville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marysville,_California "Marysville, California") and [Yuba City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuba_City,_California "Yuba City, California") in the north, and [Fresno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fresno "Fresno") and [Bakersfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakersfield "Bakersfield") in the south. [California State Highway 160](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Route_160 "California State Route 160") approaches the city after running along the [Sacramento River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") from [Contra Costa County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contra_Costa_County,_California "Contra Costa County, California") in the south and then becomes a major city street in [Downtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") before turning into the North Sacramento Freeway, going over the [American River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River "American River") to Business 80.

Some Sacramento neighborhoods, such as Downtown Sacramento and [Midtown Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento") are very bicycle friendly as are many other communities in the region. As a result of litigation, Sacramento has undertaken to make all city facilities and sidewalks wheelchair accessible. In an effort to preserve its urban neighborhoods, Sacramento has constructed [traffic-calming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traffic_calming "Traffic calming") measures in many areas.

### Rail service

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Rail service")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sacramento_Valley_Station_%28cropped2%29.JPG/250px-Sacramento_Valley_Station_%28cropped2%29.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Valley_Station_(cropped2).JPG) The historic [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station"), utilized by [Amtrak California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California"), is a gateway to the [Sacramento Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley").

[Amtrak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak "Amtrak") provides passenger rail service to the city of Sacramento. The [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station") is on the corner of 5th and I streets near the historic Old Town Sacramento and underwent extensive renovations in 2007. The station serves as a [SacRT light rail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SacRT_light_rail "SacRT light rail") terminus.

[Amtrak California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California") operates the _[Capitol Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitol_Corridor_(Amtrak) "Capitol Corridor (Amtrak)")_, a multiple-frequency service providing service from the capital city to its northeastern suburbs and the [San Francisco Bay Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area").[\[167\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-170)

Sacramento is the northern terminus of the [Amtrak California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California") _[Gold Runner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gold_Runner "Gold Runner")_ route which provides direct multiple-frequency passenger rail service to California's Central Valley as far as [Bakersfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakersfield,_California "Bakersfield, California"); [Amtrak Thruway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak_Thruway "Amtrak Thruway") connections are available from the trains at Bakersfield to [Southern California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California") and Southern [Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nevada "Nevada"). An additional service under this banner is expected to be routed through Midtown in 2026.[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-ModestoACE-171)

Sacramento is a stop along Amtrak's _[Coast Starlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast_Starlight "Coast Starlight")_ route which provides scenic service to [Seattle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle "Seattle") via [Klamath Falls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klamath_Falls,_Oregon "Klamath Falls, Oregon") and [Portland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portland,_Oregon "Portland, Oregon") to the north and Los Angeles via [San Luis Obispo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Luis_Obispo,_California "San Luis Obispo, California") and [Santa Barbara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California "Santa Barbara, California") to the south.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Sacramento_WP_station%2C_October_2006.jpg/250px-Sacramento_WP_station%2C_October_2006.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_WP_station,_October_2006.jpg) The historic [Sacramento Western Pacific station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_station_(Western_Pacific_Railroad) "Sacramento station (Western Pacific Railroad)") was served by the _[California Zephyr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Zephyr_(1949%E2%80%931970) "California Zephyr (1949–1970)")_ until 1970.

Amtrak's _[California Zephyr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Zephyr "California Zephyr")_ serves Sacramento daily and provides service to the east serving [Reno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reno,_Nevada "Reno, Nevada"), [Salt Lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_Utah "Salt Lake City, Utah"), [Denver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver "Denver"), [Omaha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska "Omaha, Nebraska"), [Chicago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago "Chicago"), and intermediate cities.

[Sacramento Valley Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Station "Sacramento Valley Station") provides numerous Amtrak Thruway routes. One route serves the cities of [Marysville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marysville,_California "Marysville, California"), [Oroville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oroville,_California "Oroville, California"), [Chico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chico,_California "Chico, California"), [Corning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corning,_California "Corning, California"), [Red Bluff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Bluff,_California "Red Bluff, California"), and [Redding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redding,_California "Redding, California") with additional service to [Yreka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yreka,_California "Yreka, California") and even [Medford, Oregon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medford,_Oregon "Medford, Oregon"). A second serves the cities of [Roseville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roseville,_California "Roseville, California"), [Rocklin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocklin,_California "Rocklin, California"), [Auburn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auburn,_California "Auburn, California"), [Colfax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colfax,_California "Colfax, California"), [Truckee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truckee,_California "Truckee, California"), Reno, and [Sparks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sparks,_Nevada "Sparks, Nevada"). The third and final Amtrak Thruway route serves [Placerville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placerville,_California "Placerville, California"), [Lake Tahoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Tahoe "Lake Tahoe"), [Stateline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stateline,_Nevada "Stateline, Nevada") Casinos, and [Carson City, Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carson_City,_Nevada "Carson City, Nevada"). Each of these routes provides multiple frequencies each day.

Sacramento has the second busiest Amtrak station in California and the seventh busiest in the country.[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-172)

[Altamont Corridor Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altamont_Corridor_Express "Altamont Corridor Express") [commuter rail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") service is expected to be routed through Sacramento in 2026.[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-ModestoACE-171) This service will utilize the [Union Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_Pacific "Union Pacific")'s [Sacramento Subdivision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Subdivision "Sacramento Subdivision"), the route of the original _California Zephyr_, where additional passenger capacity is available.[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-NewService-173)

Sacramento is expected to serve as the northern terminus of the [California High-Speed Rail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_High-Speed_Rail "California High-Speed Rail") system.

### Airport

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Airport")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sacramento_Airport%2C_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633188.tif/lossy-page1-250px-Sacramento_Airport%2C_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633188.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacramento_Airport,_Sacramento,_California_LCCN2013633188.tif) [Sacramento International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport")

[Sacramento International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport") ( [IATA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IATA_airport_code "IATA airport code"): **SMF**, [ICAO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICAO_airport_code "ICAO airport code"): **KSMF**, [FAA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration "Federal Aviation Administration") [LID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Location_identifier "Location identifier"): **SMF**) is a public [airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airport "Airport") 10 miles (16 kilometers) northwest of downtown Sacramento, in [Sacramento County, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_County,_California "Sacramento County, California"). [Southwest Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwest_Airlines "Southwest Airlines") is the dominant passenger airline with more than 104 daily flights to 25 cities across the US.[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-174) Other airlines include [Delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines "Delta Air Lines"), [United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Airlines "United Airlines"), [Spirit Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirit_Airlines "Spirit Airlines"), [American Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Airlines "American Airlines") and [Alaska Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Airlines "Alaska Airlines"). The airport handles flights to and from various US destinations (including Hawaii) as well as Mexico, Canada and connecting flights to Europe, Asia, and South America, and served more than 13 million passengers in 2019.[\[172\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-175) The airport is well known for the 56-foot-long (17 m) red aluminum rabbit titled "Leap" by [Lawrence Argent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrence_Argent "Lawrence Argent") in Terminal B.[\[173\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-176)

[McClellan Airfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_McClellan_Airport "Sacramento McClellan Airport") ( [IATA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IATA_airport_code "IATA airport code"): **MCC**, [ICAO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICAO_airport_code "ICAO airport code"): **KMCC**, [FAA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration "Federal Aviation Administration") [LID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Location_identifier "Location identifier"): **MCC**) is a privately owned, public-use [airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airport "Airport") that is mainly used for general aviation. It is located in the unincorporated area of [McClellan Park, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McClellan_Park,_California "McClellan Park, California"), six miles (9.7 km; 5.2 nmi) northeast of the [central business district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_business_district "Central business district") of Sacramento. The airport is on the former site of **[McClellan Air Force Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base "McClellan Air Force Base")**, and was transferred to Sacramento County in 2000. The airport is a public-use facility which operates as an uncontrolled airfield in what the FAA designates as Class "E" Airspace.

### Transit

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Transit")\]

[![A blue light rail train pulling into Mather Field/Mills station.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LightrailMather.jpg/250px-LightrailMather.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LightrailMather.jpg) The [SacRT lightrail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SacRT_light_rail "SacRT light rail") pulling into [Mather Field/Mills station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mather_Field/Mills_station "Mather Field/Mills station").

The city and its suburbs are served by [Sacramento Regional Transit District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Regional_Transit_District "Sacramento Regional Transit District"), which ranks as [the eleventh busiest in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_Light_Rail_systems_by_ridership "List of United States Light Rail systems by ridership"). Sac RT is a bus and light-rail system, with 274 buses and 76 light-rail vehicles providing service for 58,200 daily passengers. The three light-rail lines (Blue, Gold, & Green) is a 42.9 mi (69.0 km) system with 54 stations. The Gold Line was extended east as far as the city of [Folsom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folsom,_California "Folsom, California"), and more recently the Blue Line was extended south from Meadowview Rd to [Cosumnes River College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College "Cosumnes River College"). Sacramento's light rail system goes to the [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station"), [Cosumnes River College Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College_(Sacramento_RT) "Cosumnes River College (Sacramento RT)") in south Sacramento, and north to Watt/I-80 where [I-80](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I-80 "I-80") and Business 80 meeting. The light-rail Blue & Gold Lines have 15-minute weekday headways and 30-minute weekday evening and weekend/holiday headways; the Green Line has 30-minute weekday headways and no weekend service. Route 142 is an express bus line to/from [downtown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") to Sacramento International Airport.[\[174\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-Bus_Route_Webpage-177) There are expansion plans to extend the Green Line to the [airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport") and the Blue Line to the City of [Roseville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roseville,_California "Roseville, California") through the City of [Citrus Heights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citrus_Heights,_California "Citrus Heights, California"). [Yolobus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolobus "Yolobus") provides bus service to [West Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California") and [Yolo County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolo_County,_California "Yolo County, California").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Delta_King.JPG/250px-Delta_King.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Delta_King.JPG) [Old Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento")'s riverfront docks

[Greyhound Lines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greyhound_Lines "Greyhound Lines") provides intercity bus service to Portland, Reno, Los Angeles, and San Francisco from its new station along Richards Boulevard. Intercity bus service to San Francisco and [Sparks, Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sparks,_Nevada "Sparks, Nevada") is offered by [Megabus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megabus_(North_America) "Megabus (North America)").[\[175\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-178)

[Bicycling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicycling "Bicycling") is an increasingly popular transportation mode in Sacramento, which enjoys a mild climate and flat terrain. Bicycling is especially common in the older neighborhoods of Sacramento's center, such as Alkali Flat, [Midtown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento"), McKinley Park, [Land Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_Park "Land Park"), and [East Sacramento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Sacramento "East Sacramento"). Many employees who work downtown commute by bicycle from suburban communities on a dedicated bicycle path on the [American River Parkway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_River_Parkway "American River Parkway"). Sacramento was designated as a Silver Level Bicycle Friendly Community by the [League of American Bicyclists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_American_Bicyclists "League of American Bicyclists") in September 2006. The advocacy organization [Sacramento Area Bicycle Advocates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento_Area_Bicycle_Advocates "Sacramento Area Bicycle Advocates") co-sponsors the Sacramento Area Council of Governments' May is Bike Month campaign. Rideshare companies such as [Lime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lime_(transportation_company) "Lime (transportation company)"), [Bird](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird_(transportation_company) "Bird (transportation company)"), and [Helbiz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helbiz "Helbiz") have introduced up to 4,000 electric-powered scooters and bikes in Downtown Sacramento for residents to rent as a faster and alternative way to get around the city. Sacramento ranks second worldwide in ride sharable, with ridership totaling 1 million riders in 8 months.[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-179)[\[177\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-180)

There is a commuter bus service from Yolo County on [Yolobus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolobus "Yolobus"), from Solano County on [FAST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fairfield_and_Suisun_Transit "Fairfield and Suisun Transit"), on two bus lines from [Yuba County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuba_County,_California "Yuba County, California")'s [Yuba Sutter Transit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuba_Sutter_Transit "Yuba Sutter Transit"),[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-181) from [Amador](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amador_County,_California "Amador County, California") Transit's Sacramento Line,[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-182) on [Placer County Transit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placer_County_Transit "Placer County Transit")'s Auburn to Light Rail Line,[\[180\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-183) and from [San Joaquin County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Joaquin_County,_California "San Joaquin County, California") on several [SMART](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Joaquin_Regional_Transit_District "San Joaquin Regional Transit District") bus lines.

## Explanatory notes

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Explanatory notes")\]

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_ref-11 "Jump up")**


   - [American English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English "American English"): [/ˌsækrəˈmɛntoʊ/](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English")[Play audio](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/be/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Sacramento%2C_California.wav/LL-Q1860_%28eng%29-Flame%2C_not_lame-Sacramento%2C_California.wav.mp3 "Play audio")[ⓘ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Flame,_not_lame-Sacramento,_California.wav "File:LL-Q1860 (eng)-Flame, not lame-Sacramento, California.wav") [_SAK-rə-MEN-toh_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key"),[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-9)locally [/-ˈmɛnoʊ/](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [_-⁠MEN-oh_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key");[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-10)
   - Spanish:[\[sakɾaˈmento\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish "Help:IPA/Spanish"), lit.'sacrament'

2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_ref-69 "Jump up")**Official records for Sacramento were kept exclusively at the airport since 10 November 1941.[\[67\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacramento,_California#cite_note-68)

Title: Visit the State Capitol | California State Assembly
[Skip to main content](https://www.assembly.ca.gov/resources/visit-state-capitol#main-content)

# Visit the State Capitol

At the State Capitol, the past, present and future of California interact with equal force. The building serves as both a museum and the state’s working seat of government. Visitors to the Capitol can at once experience California’s rich history and witness the making of history through the modern lawmaking process.

[Find your representatives and visit their Capitol offices](https://www.assembly.ca.gov/assemblymembers/find-my-rep)

![Capitol State Building ](<Base64-Image-Removed>)

## California Capitols

Shortly after the end of Mexican rule, Californians began to clamor for statehood. In 1849, a constitutional convention met at Colton Hall in Monterey and proposed a constitution, subsequently ratified by the people, which named San Jose as the first capital.

In December 1849, the first Legislature convened in a two-story adobe hotel in San Jose. The city was composed of little more than huts, tents and clapboard buildings, and the general discomfort did little to endear the city to the legislators.In 1851 a generous offer from General Vallejo induced the legislators to move the capital to Vallejo where a frame building had been erected for their use. Since housing was virtually nonexistent, many of the Members managed to secure lodging on the steamer Empire, which remained moored at a wharf during the session.

![](<Base64-Image-Removed>)**California State Capitol** (early 1900s)

Confusion and inconvenience again brought stormy cries for relocation. After convening in Vallejo in 1852, the Legislature moved to Sacramento to finish the legislative session. In 1853, the Legislature returned to Vallejo only to find conditions as inhospitable as before. To an exasperated membership, an offer from the community of Benicia for the use of its new city hall proved irresistible, and a bill was passed moving the seat of government to that city, where the legislative session finished.

While the legislative quarters were adequate, it became increasingly evident that Benicia itself was too small to serve as the capital city. With this in mind, the Legislature determined that Sacramento would be the state’s capital and moved from Benicia in February 1854. Sacramento offered its courthouse for immediate use and a building site for the permanent Capitol. Shortly after the close of the Session of 1854, the courthouse was razed by fire, but a new one was completed in time for the next session.

The new courthouse continued to serve as the home of the Legislature until 1869. This tenure was interrupted only once; during the winter of 1861–62 a severe flood prompted removal of the Legislature to the Exchange Building in San Francisco. Construction on the permanent Capitol was begun in 1860, and, though not completed until 1874, the Legislature was able to occupy its Chambers in 1869. Except for a major “modernization” in 1908, the Capitol remained virtually unchanged until 1949 when additional space requirements resulted in the construction of the Capitol Annex. Completed in 1951, the Annex attaches to the east side of the old Capitol and houses legislative offices, committee rooms and the Governor’s offices.

In 1976, a total reconstruction of the building was undertaken to strengthen and reinforce the weakening structure. This monumental project was completed in January 1982, and the old Capitol, restored to its turn-of-the-century decor, was again occupied by the Legislature and opened to the public.

### Accessibility

Wheelchair Access

| **Location** | **Elevators** | **Wheelchair Access** |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **State Capitol**<br>1315 10th Street<br>Sacramento, CA 95814 | Elevators are located on each side of the rotunda. | The North (L Street) and South (N Street) entrances have wheelchair ramps.<br>Sidewalks leading to the Capitol are wheelchair accessible. |
| **Swing Space**<br>1021 O St.<br>Sacramento, CA 95814 | Elevators accessible to the general public are located at the back of the building after passing through security.<br>During session, wait times for elevators may be extended. Please plan your visit accordingly. | Front entrance is wheelchair accessible. |
| **Legislative Office Building (LOB)**<br>1020 N St.<br>Sacramento, CA 95814 | Elevators are located at the entrance of the building, after security. | Front entrance is wheelchair accessible. |

Title: The State Capitals - La Salle University
The capital of Alabama is Montgomery.

The capital of California is Sacramento.
